<Content>A Must - if you get a good deal Christmas in New York - Expectation were highArrived late ( 12.45am) after a long flight. Check-in was so smooth, reception staff couldn't do enough for us. We had asked for a fridge in our room (which can be requested F.O.C). This they sent up as soon as we arrived.Knowing that Tea/Coffee making facilities where not available in the room we packed a kettle. So on arrival we asked for some milk and the bar staff fell over themselves to accommodate our request.The room was very clean (just a little dated) the beds were so comfortable we didn't want to get out of them.There is a very good deli next door where you can buy breakfast / Salads, very good sandwiches  cakes. Great to take up to room after a long day walking around New York.24hr Pharmacy (sells all sorts) just on the corner.You can easily walk to Times square (10 - 15 mins) and the metro is just 2 mins, which will take you all over (at a very good price of $24 for the week).If I had one criticism it would be the restaurant. Food poor  costly, staff require more customer Service training.Oliver Tree (Time Square) for an Italian meal is a must. Quality food at a very reasonable price. Staff lovelyWe are looking forward to going back next year!

<Author>Erin_Dan
<Content>Average Stay at the Helmsley Our arrival at the Helmsley was at about midnight and after 8hrs on a plane, were looking forward to getting to the hotel and grabbing a coffee or a bite. From outside it looks like something out of a film, very bling, if not a bit seventies.Arriving at the hotel: the doorman let us struggle through the door with our own bags, not a great start, and the woman behind the desk acted most upset that she had to deal with some customers. Her manner was poor, bordering on rude, when she laid down the law about how she would charge my credit card for potential damage to the room which, she was eluding to, was the 'approval' to see if the credit on the card was good. My faith in the hotel was falling.We asked if we could get a drink.... No was the answer. The bar was shut, room service was closed too and she didn't know of anywhere nearby to get a drink at that hour. By the way, we'd visited NYC before and knew that there would be somewhere - we just didnt know where in that neighbourhood and found somewhere a few days later.Our first room on the 19th floor, was cold, had broken heat, an even more broken door lock that took many to open (we went down to reception and it took 15min for anyone to show). The room was okay - broken hairdrier, good view, nice TV, great bed, though it was a little shabby. A call down to reception about the heat was ignored.Next morning we showered, in the cold (it was 13F outside so the room wasn't much more) and headed down to reception. We complained and was told that these issues would be resolved immediately. They weren't. Most of the reception staff didn't care and had to look up simple info like when the bar was supposed to be open etc.It took several more calls and a final visit to reception when the issue was finally escalated and we were moved to the 31st floor to a better (less broken) but smaller room with a better view.The new room solved most of the issues, though the doorlock was still intermittently faulty - a fault most of the other guests we spoke to seemed to agree with. The director also kindly sent a bottle of bubbly to try make it right which we appreciated and went some way to salvaging our trip.To be honest, we were so tired of complaining that we left the remaining issues outstanding as it was really spoiling our trip.Room service was dire at all times. Always at least 35+ minutes if you wanted just a coffee (no facilities in the room) and the bar regularly didnt have coffee (this is NYC for Christ's sake!). Lucky there were 2 starbucks within a block or two though it was very dissapointing not to be able to have breakfast in bed a couple of times or at least a drink before setting out.If you have to stay here, I'd recommend the mini market on 2nd ave (right out of the hotel, right again onto second and it's on the right). And for breakfast - also on Second Ave - the Townhouse Cafe had the NICEST staff and the food was great value. On the left hand side, a couple of blocks down on the left hand side of second.Conclusion. Wouldn't stay here. The Helmsley wasn't cheap and last year we paid a little more for the Hilton Times Square which was light years better in terms of facilities and service. Unless there's big improvements, I won't be staying here again.

<Author>Raz868
<Content>Great hotel in great location I stayed here with my girlfriend for one week in mid december. We absolutely loved the stay here, apart from a few hassels with the room(which I will get to later). Location of this hotel is so great, in east midtown on a busy street(42th) with aprox 15-20 min walk to times square and 25-30 min walk to central park. The hotel is right next to Chrysler Building and Grand Central Terminal, which is great for the subway (which we didnt use much of, instead we walked pretty much everywhere, location being so convenient)Our room was very huge and just great; we had two double beds (the biggest and most comfortable beds ever), a near spotless bathroom with a huge bathtub, a flat screen tv, and big windows which made the room well lit up. We did however had some issues though; there was a problem with the toilet and upon arrival the windows couldn't be sealed shut, resulting in some noise from traffic the first night, even being on 33rd floor(im a very light sleeper). The next day we spoke to reception and there was a guy to help us in 5 minutes. People at front desk were very kind, helping with all kind of questions. Very nice.There was a restaurant at the hotel that looked nice; we never tried it though as we always ate out. Same with breakfast, we took food from PAX next door(cheap and good) to our hotel room, or went to Pershing Square (not cheap but good) right opposite Grand Central Terminal. Pershing Square also had good valuable lunch and dinner. There's also a good mexican restaurant near the hotel which is recommended; it's called El Rio Grande and it's on 38th street just off 3th ave.I highly recommend this hotel for it being so good located, the friendliness of the staff and the cleanliness and high standard of the rooms. Me and my girlfriend had our best vacation in NY and hope to return; there were simply so many things that we didnt have time to do while there, new york city truly is an amazing place.

<Author>LillianLM
<Content>Excellent value I booked this hotel a few weeks ago on hotels.com, with a rate of $200 plus taxes, which is an unbelieveable rate for the weekend before Christmas (which is actually a sad indication of the state of the economy). The location was very good, although I prefer to stay closer to 5th Avenue but at this room rate, I happily walked. The room was relatively big for a Manhattan hotel room and very clean. The furnishing were a bit outdated but the bed was terrific, with excellent linens. I felt secure -- after 9 pm you must show your room key to security before getting onto the elevator. We were directed by the dorrman to an inexpensive Greek diner for breakfast called Joe's, on the corner of 2nd Avenue and 44th street (2 1/2 blocks from the hotel), Check-out was a breeze and we had no problems leaving our luggage with the bellman for 5 hours after checking out while we walked around. Extremely polite staff -- all in all, an excellent stay.

<Author>G0retti
<Content>Was not disappointed Just back from 6 nights at this hotel and have to say it came up to my expectations of a good quality hotel. The lobby area when you come in first was very impressive, porters very attentive and girls on reception very friendly. The plush red carpet and the carpeting throughout the hotel was excellent. The rooms were upmarket, and I felt like I was being pampered staying at this hotel.I stayed on the 8th floor and found the room very comfortable, heating just right. We could turn it off if we got too hot by a switch on the wall and we could open the window if we needed fresh air.I never heard any traffic or noise as I slept at night, as reported by others on this site. My daughter and son were staying on the street side of the hotel and they had the same experience.Now the only thing I did not like was the food, but that was not particular to this hotel. The dining room had a nice ambience though and the waiters very professional. I found that most of the food in New York was greasy, heavy and sickening.The location is very central and I would have no hesitation in recommending this hotel to my friends and would certainly go back again.

<Content>Great Location Stayed at the Helmsley on a 7 night girls holiday to New York. We booked this hotel after reading reviews on trip advisor and were not disappointed. The best part of this hotel was its location. We were a couple of hundred metres from Grand Central Station where you can get the subway or a quick bite to eat. There is good deli right next door to the hotel which did lovely bacon and egg rolls. For a more formal breakfast there is a sit down restaurant directly opposite Grand Central Station. I can recomend the New Yorker breakfast. The hotel is only a 15mins walk from the Empire State Building, and about the same to Times Square. The hotel itself is clean and friendly. Four of us stayed in one room and had plently of space. We had 2 queen size beds in the room which were big enough to share. There was a safe in the wardrope and radio which we could dock with our ipod. There was a hairdryer in the bathroom which was fine, and UK GHD hair straightners worked fine. The only thing we found a bit awkward was the fact that the only miror by a plug socket was in the bathroom, so with four girls getting reading at the same time there was a bit of waiting around. But this was not really a big problem. Drinks are fairly expensive in the hotel bar, about $7.5 for a beer, $8.5 for a vodka and coke and $9.5 for a baileys (thats without tax or tip). There is a 24 hour chemist a few doors down from the hotel and plenty of banks on the walk from the hotel to Grand Central Station. I would recommend buying a tour bus ticket from the hotel. We got an all loops tour for $49 which lasts for 48hours. We did the downtown loop where we saw the Empire State Building, Flatiron building, Ground Zero, China Town, South Street Sea Port etc. We walked across the Brooklyn Bridge and picked up the Brooklyn Tour bus. The only problem was that we could not find the bus stop and got lost in the wrong area! Eventually we caught the bus along Cadmen Plaza West at Clark Street. We also did the uptown loop which took us around Central Park and Harlem. For a bit of fun you can wave at the earth cam outside TGI Fridays on Times Square so people back home can see you. Best highlights apart from shopping were: Empire State Building, Statue of Liberty, Top of the Rock at night, watching the Little Mermaid on Broadway and ice skating in Central Park. The hotel was in a great location to fit all of this in comfortably.  
<Date>Dec 7, 2008

<Author>Oz1Sydney
<Content>The Helmsley really grew on us! Just be aware that there seem to be different grade rooms available. We checked in after midnight and were told there were no King deluxe rooms available, despite requesting and paying for one in advance. The room we were given, on the 16th floor was very disappointing. It had 2 double beds and the decor was very tired. The carpet was dirty and very stained and the pillows smelt old and smoky. There were no glasses, just plastic cups. This just didn't feel right?!The next morning we asked to change rooms. The lady on reception was very friendly and helpful. We were moved to the 22nd floor and the room was a 100% improvement - clean, spacious and very comfortable.Although the decor is in a bit of a 1980s timewarp, the Helmsley is a great hotel. It's in a good location, with a comfortable bar area and good cafes and restaurants just a short stroll away.

<Author>BOHSMAN
<Content>GREAT LOCATION This was our second visit to the New York Helmsley, and our first with kids. I had e-mailed the reservations dept in advance requesting a high floor room and this was granted. We had a room on the 29th floor which was of an sufficient size for our needs. Only problem was that it was impossible to cool, even withthe air con to minimum, or windows open ( with air con off . We did'nt eat in the hotel restaurant as we felt that breakfast in PAX diner next door was better value and also a real NYC experience ( NEXT!!!!!!! ). We ate in HARRYS BAR at lunchtime once and would have done so again except the portions are quite large which did'nt leave much room for dinner at night. that said, everyone was very happy with their food. The fries are to die for --- nicest i've tasted in a while. At night, the lobby/ bar area can be quite cold due to the constant pedestrian traffic through the doors. This hotel is superbly located, being approx 5mins walk from Grand Central Station, and we would certainly stay here again. Also, i had read on these pages about the supposed attitude of the security people at the lift area at night but our experience was that these guys were very friendly, polite, a reassuring presence, etc., We will be back.

<Author>THETRUEMEZ
<Content>The best in New York!! When we were planning our trip to New York we were very apprehensive BUT this Hotel is absolutely the best place to stay. The rooms are very spacious and all appear to have been refurbished to a high standard. The bed is huge and super comfortable, pillows great, air conditioning and heating [all through one unit] was great too.The bathroom gives you choice of tub or shower and the towels are high quality. The room has a safe and hair dryer and 'his and hers' dressing gowns and if you request it, they will send a refrigerator up to you room and set it up [invaluable for your bottled water, beer/wine for the room]. Once your reservation is confirmed send them and email request for the refrigerator before you travel and it will be on their system when you check in. They do not provide tea or coffee making facilities but room service will provide this for you all day long and not expensive. We were on the 29th floor and there was virtually zero traffic/horn blowing noise. The lifts are high speed and with six lifts runnig all the time, you have no waiting about, even on a busy check out period. We had booked an Executive King Room through 'Hotels.com' but you can book direct through the Hotel too. The staff are excellent in every respect. The bell hops are cheary guys and whilst you need to tip them all, it is part of the New York experience. A guy called Bernado checked us in and he was mega polite and helpful; but so was every member of hotel staff that we spoke to. They gave us a voucher for a free bottle of wine if we dined in the Hotel Restaurant, which we did on the first night and the ambiance and food in the restaurant was superb; The food was excellent and we both went for the New York stripp steak-one cooked medium and one well done and they were both cooked to perfection. The free bottle of wine was a superb bottle of Chardonnay [there was a choice] and it was not expensive in our view.The Restaurant Captain was very attentive and a most pleasant guy with a good sense of humour.The concierge was excellent and advised on all local restaurants/ Diners and sight seeing and marked up maps for you- we went one evening to 'O'Niels Irish Bar and Restaurant' a stroll from the Hotel and had a great evening there and had Dublin Bangers with Mash and Onions and it was great -very reasonably priced BUT very busy in the dining area -all the food that we saw served up looked super.Back at the hotel, the concierge checked out our train departures for Long Island and were most helpful.The Helmsley Hotel is located at 212 East 42nd Street and it was, in our view, a super location to get around. Checking out was also a painless experience.SO, IF YOU ARE GOING TO NEW YORK DEFINATELY STAY HERE- IT IS BRILLIANT!!A couple of other things you might find of assistance:Getting a cab between 4pm and 8pm can be a pain but be patient. DO NOT take a non yellow cab-plenty of Lincoln type cars will stop and wave a taxi card at you but these are unregulated in New York and are not recommended to use as you can get ripped off big time. The yellow cabs are pretty cheap [compared to London Black Cabs]If you are going to New York for the first time, mixing sight seeing and shopping is a mighty task to undertake and you are on the go every hour of every day; if you can, spread it over 4 days minimum and it is then both manageable and enjoyable that way. We highly recommend the Gray Lines open top Red Buses which are 'hop on hop off' BUT buy the tickets on line first as it is cheaper [from the UK anyway] We paid $44 each for a 2 day pass which was great value and gave us 48 hour access to the three loops. These were 'Uptown loop' [Central Park and Harlem etc]'Downtown Loop' which covers all the rest of NY Sights and then the 'Brooklyn loop' but we did not go on this last loop due to lack of time [needed an extra day for this really]. The ticket also included the night tour which is NOT hop on hop off. Once on it, it lasts about 2 hours seeing the NY Skyline lit up. With the Gray Lines 48 hour ticket you also get a free ticket for the NY Water taxis so you can get over to see the Statue of Liberty. BE AWARE that you will queue for these buses but it only takes a 20 to 30 minute wait max and you get on -everybody wants to be on the top deck of course so it takes a while for the buses to get around through traffic -there are other bus service providers but Gray Lines are the best. We do recommend that you take the Staten Island ferry -it's free and you get the best views of Manhattan and Ellis Island and the Staue of Liberty and it only takes 20 minutes each way with the boats running all the itmeALSO, if you want theatre tickets DO NOT book these at home. Go to the Marriot hotel in Times Square and go the the ticket office there as the tickets are half price.If you want to go up the Empire State Building, get there for 9.30 or 10am or you will dislike the queues and crowding- early is the very best time to visit and worth the money for the experience and the view. GIRLS -if you want UGG Boots there is a shop called DAVID Z.COM yards from the Empire State [there are a few in NY-check it out on line before you travel] and they have a great selection PLUS they do the Classic tall boot for $167 INC TAX and this is about $40 cheaper than Bloomingdales.Also, if the GUYS like Cons or Vans, these are cheap here too -Converse about $43 INC TAXIf you want super cheap designer gear you MUST go to 'CENTURY 21' which is opposite Ground Zero/World Trade Centre site. Top designers really really cheap BUT be warned it is VERY busy in there with serious buyers. IF you are travelling on Long Island, we recommend both the LIRR Railway [you get it from Penn Station under Madison Square Garden] -it is very clean and safe as every train has guards/ticket collectors and it is easy to use. It runs ON TIME!! Also, if you want to see Long Island [if you are going up to the Hamptons] try the 'Hampton Jitney' -a luxery coach and whilst twice the train fare, it is very efficient and good views.Check it out on line for time of trains and buses -it's dead easy and again, they ALL run on time.If you do go up to Montauk, at the tip of Long Island, check out the light house and the local views BUT for the best dining go to the 'HARVEST ON FORT POND' this is a real food experience. Not only is this a superb restaurant and very nice ambiance, the food is very different is two respects - Firstly, the food is most excellent in every way but Secondly, this is a 'family meal restaurant' which means that when you order sometihng a HUGE PORTION arrives and it is for the family to share -it is not recommended to try this restaurant unless there is a minimum of Four or you will need to take away a dooggie bag [or doggie carrier bag]. This goes for all items on the menu, so when you see a Pizza for $17 DO NOT think it is for one -it is HUGE. Again, if you are going to Long Island make a day to visit a TANGER OUTLET [we went to the RIVERHEAD Location] - this is dying and going to shopping heaven and ALL at major discounts and I kid you not on that one!!! BUT BE WARNED - It is massive in size and it will take you all day to get around it -plently of choice to eat in the food court though. We recommend a car to get to this place by the way and it is a LONG WAY from central New York and not a a day trip.Well, we hope that helps any of you that have hotel choice concerns and especially if it is your first trip to New York. It is a great place to visit BUT if you do not plan it properly, it could be a nightmare -SO spend some time on the internet and plan your trip -REMEMBER to take trainers or good walking shoes because NY is vast and what seems short on the map is not quite as short as you think it is. Last thing if you live in the UK -get the 'AA Guide to New York' -easy to carry and invaluable -it was the best thing we invested in and a week or so pre-read helped us plan a memerable trip.GOOD LUCK  HAVE FUN!!!!!!!

<Author>TravelDrew
<Content>If you want a great hotel, this ISN'T it! The New York Helmsley may have been a nice hotel at one time, but that time is long gone. This is a worn and tired hotel, with old rooms, old carpet, old painting, and old bedding. While the newish flat screen TV in the rooms may convince some that this is a modern hotel, it serves the same function as lipstick on a pig.The hotel staff was, quite frankly, rude. My wife and I checked in, unfortunately, at the same time a large group was checking out. Instead of attempting to help the group, or individual travelers such as my wife and I, many members of the hotel staff decided to hide in their glass enclosed offices. When I confronted one, asking for help, he responded, I'm busy. Then went to play with something on his computer screen. Check-in took more than 20 minutes. Several times during our stay, the keycard reader for our room became inoperable, requiring a trek down to the main lobby (40 floors down), to have a new key issued. This is unacceptable in a major hotel.Checkout was also no breeze. The rate charged was HIGHER than the rate initialed at check in. The manager denied the rate was different, but upon my demand that she find the paper that I initialed, she admitted that there was a mistake. Be warned: look very closely a the rate your initialing. This hotel seems to play fast and loose with rates. Bottom line: I would NOT recommend this hotel to anyone. It needs to be renovated, and the staff needs to be overhauled.

<Content>We had the Holiday of a Lifetime !!! We (family of four) have just returned home after staying for a week at the Helmsley and had the holiday of a lifetime, all of the previous reviews/photos on tripadvisor really helped us.Staff very friendly and helpful, location brilliant ie very near to Grand Central, we purchased 7 day subway/bus metro cards for $25 each (real bargin).Fausto the bell hop a top-man with great tips of where to eat breakfast (try the Comfy Diner a couple of blocks north from 42nd street) or Dinner (try Palm Too if you like lobster/steaks).Get your coffee from next door in the local PAX take-away as no tea/ coffee making facilities in hotel rooms (no real hasstle for us). Concierge were really helpful as well booking (with the personal touch) e.g. limo to take us back to Airport, helicopter flights etc (with costs the same as you would get elsewhere).Our rooms were on the 26th floor in the rear of the Hotel looking over the Empire State Building......fabWe would have no hesitation in recommending this Hotel. <Author>weski
<Content>4th of July Madness My son and I stayed for the 4th of July to see the Fireworks. The hotel was filled to the fills, with many, many foreigners in the for holiday. The line to checkin went to the door, but did move. We stayed on the 22nd floor in a double-double. It was fine - comfortable clean beds, decent, but not glamerous bathroom. Overlooked 41st Street - not a problem. Comfy chair, desk, flat screen TV. TIP for 4th of July - We thought we would get a bite around 7 pm before the 9 pm fireworks. The street was already packed with people lining up to get through the checkpoints (at 42nd St) to go down by the FDR Drive to see the fireworks. All the nearby restaurants, bars, etc. were filled with waiting lines. We got in line and went down to the river. We stood in amongth thousands of our closest friends behind the chain link fences and jersey walls until 9:30 when the fireworks finally went off. In hindsight, while we were close to the 42nd St. entrance, I would recommend going down near the Seaport for a better view of the fireworks - there are 3 barges in the East River, but we saw it all as one big mash - in the distance. A great disappointment - no music, just a crush. Then made our way back to the hotel - thank goodness it was nearby, but we were thirsy and starving, like everyone else. The line to the restaurant was huge, so we lined up for the bar. Got in, finally, had multiple cold drinks and a small pizza and quesdilla - they were fine. Went to bed. Checkout fine. Don't have to do this again, but if I do, it will be downtown or on someone's downtown roof.

<Author>NewYorkGroove
<Content>Great Affortable Stay I stayed at the Helmsley in mid-July 2008 and I can't say enough good things about it. The hotel is located about three blocks east of Grand Central Station, so you don't have a far walk to get to the train. The cab ride there from LaGuardia was about $25, which isn't too bad. The area is quite safe and busy most of the time, so you don't have to be afraid of walking back to your room, even late at night. The hotel is located only a couple blocks away from the Empire State Building, and you are only a shuttle train away from Times Square. The staff was excellent, from the front desk staff to the bellmen. The rooms were nice and decent-sized. I was lucky enough to snag a room on the southeast corner of the hotel, so the room was probably a little bigger than most of the other rooms. I had a problem when I checked in, when my room keys would not open the door. The person at the front desk promptly issued me two new keys and the problem was solved. Overall, a wonderful stay. My stay lasted six days and I feel I got a lot for my money. I would not hesitate to stay at the Helmsley again, and in fact, I plan on staying there during my next visit to NY.

<Author>Archie24
<Content>Excellent location, great view! Great central location, pretty good value too. We stayed for 5 nights and got a great room on 41st floor overlooking the Chrysler building - not good for someone who's scared of heights but I got used to it! Agree with other reviewers that it's better value to avoid hotel breakfast and go to Pax Deli next door, where you can get excellent breakfasts for half the price. Good little gym in the hotel, which always seemed quiet - only a few facilities in there but enough equipment to be able to work off the bagels every morning. The concierge (Frank, I think) was excellent and recommended great restaurants in the neighbourhood on the nights we were too tired to venture back downtown. Dean's Pizza round the corner on 2nd Ave was pretty good value for basic Italian or there's a great little Chinese place on 39th (from memory) where you can bring your own booze.We walked from the hotel to most nearby attractions - Grand Central, Times Square, Empire State building (a bit further away but still around 15 mins walk). Subway lines 4,5,6 from Grand Central take you direct to most of the useful touristy places - uptown to the museums or downtown to Wall Street, South St seaport, Brooklyn Bridge.

<Author>nic_leb
<Content>Doesn't Disappoint Stayed at the Helmsley for two nights in June of 2008 for a leisure weekend in the city with my spouse. The hotel is a favorite of my in-laws and I wasn't disappointed. We had a quiet corner king room with a nice bay window on an upper floor. Room size was surprisingly good for an NYC hotel. The hotel staff were courteous and helpful. I have to say that the Helmsley is looking a little dated in its decor, BUT the hotel is IMPECCABLY maintained. Nothing that I saw or encountered was spotted, torn, stained, chipped or inoperable. The bathroom had a marble-topped vanity with many large towels and a handy magnifying mirror. There isn't a mini bar in the room, but there's a nice drugstore just down at the corner in case you need anything.The location is fabulous, walkable to the Public Library, Bryant Park, Grand Central, Times Square, Broadway shows, and all the mid-town attractions!

<Author>NCWorldTraveler
<Content>Great Customer Service Three friends and I stayed at the New York Helmsley from May 22-May 25. When we arrived we were immediately greeted by a hotel employee who helped us with our bags and parked the car. He was extremely pleasant. Inside we did not have to wait on line to check-in as they were ample employees on hand. Check in was a breeze and the bell hop took us up to our room. He too was very nice. I saw complaints from others on this site about the dated furniture. Certainly, the furnishings are not comparable to that of the W hotel, for instance, but it was still very nice and the room was clean. For the entire stay, housekeeping, the concierge, and all of the employees we encountered were wonderful. The location is ideal. It is just a couple of blocks away from Grand Central Station and surrounded by great restaurants. There are also a few Starbucks' close by. It is an easy walk to Times Square, shopping on 5th Avenue and Bryant Park as well as the NY Public Library. There is also a great workout room that I utilized while there. Fresh towels and bottled waters are readily available. There are also security cameras that provide a level of comfort if you are working out alone. The only negative thing I have to say is that the cost of the breakfast buffet was very high. I don't remember the exact price was but there is a restaurant right next door that serves and awesome breakfast at reasonable rates. Overall it was great stay and I would definitely stay there again!

<Author>TheGazz
<Content>A VERY Pleasant Surprise I travel almost every other week to NYC and I had never stayed at a Helmsley Property. I did not think they were my style (on the boutique/contemporary side), and there was just something about the Queen of Mean that made me NOT want to stay at her hotels. Well -- between the fact that there was a great rate on Travelzoo and the Queen of Mean is no longer...I decided to give it a try. My expectation was that it would be a very snobby and stuffy environment ---boy was I wrong.I book on Travelzoo frequently, and I often get the associated low level of service for the low price (second class citizen treatment). Not here...from the minute I walked in, EVERY person I came in contact with---be it front desk, car attendents, hotel operator, or housekeeping -- they all bent over backward with friendly and attentive service missing from so many other hotels in NYC. I arrived at 11:00 AM---fully expecting no room availability because I was so early. I really intended just to leave my bag, but I said ---what the hell -- let me give it a try. They were happy to both give me a room AND satisfy my request for a high floor --- the 38th. While the room was not my style --- it was stylish -- and a great size with a great size bathroom. A little dated, yes. Could use a bit of renovation, yes. But it had everytrhing you needed, all in good working order, and very clean. I'm so used to the snobby, let me do you a favor by allowing you to stay at my property cold shoulder treatment at so many NYC hotels ( i.e. Flatotel, Waldorf Astoria, Intercontinental Barclay, The London, etc.) that attitude and service count alot for me. I'm willing to overlook alot of little things when a hotel has that right. Yes, the location is great, the rooms are large, and the ameneties are nice -- but for me, it was the PEOPLE at the Helmsley New York that made it a truely enjoyable experience. I would not hesitate to stay here, or other Hrlmsley properties, ever again. She may have been mean -- but it looks to me like they are celebrating their freedom!!!!!

<Author>Traveleasier
<Content>New York - What an amazing place Arrived in New York from JFK courtesy of a limo from Lincoln Limousines ($65 one way - trip was easy, car was in need of an update). Pulled up to the hotel, went to the front desk and we were greeted by Doris who started off our trip perfectly. Big smile, easy check in process (our room was not ready so we just checked the bags) and then Doris pretty much took us under her wing. She pulled out the map of Manhattan and pretty much planned out trip for the next four days. It was like having your own tour guide. She was just amazing and her routes were fantastic. If you want to experience New York, just make sure that you speak to her. She gave us some insider tips (take the Staten Island ferry to see the Statue of Liberty since apparently, you can no longer go inside. The ferry is free.) and recommended some great places to eat (try Sarge's Deli, 548 3rd Ave, between 36th Ave and 37th Ave). Hotel was very nice although the rooms could probably use a bit of updating. We stayed on the 31st floor overlooking 42nd Street. Room was fine with a king sized bed, flat panel TV, regular sized bathroom and in room safe. Apart from the street noise (just typical New York with sirens blaring and horns honking) and the occasional door closing (not sure why it is necessary to make doors so heavy that when they close, other rooms shake. Be nice to your neighbours and gently help the door close.), everything was fine. We did not eat in the hotel or use any of the facilities (there are a couple of computers for guest usage but they cost). There is a restaurant just beside the hotel for breakfasts and light lunches and it will suit most people just fine. Hotel is really well situated about 5 minutes walking to/from Grand Central and probably about 15-20 minutes walking to/from Times Square. Use the New York subway. It's a great way to get around and better than taxis for the most part. Traffic in New York is just unbelievable, all hours of the day. All in all, it was just a fantastic stay and although Doris was not working on the day that we left, her smile left with us. Stay at the Helmsley, it's worth it.  
<Date>May 15, 2008

<Content>Great location, dirty rooms Leona is surely turning over in her grave. Since we spent no time at all in our room we didn't use the amenities at the hotel, (gym and restaurant) we did have some nightcaps at the pleasant bar in the lobby.We were drawn to the Helmsley for the reasonable (for NYC) price and locale and since we walked or cabbed everywhere I can't let you know about the convenience to the subway but Grand Central Terminal is about a block away with the Theater district about 7 blocks in the other direction. I may or may not stay there again, it would depend on what I was in NYC to accomplish. If you aren't planning on staying in your room much and aren't squeamish about floor cleanliness bring slippers and consider this hotel if you are looking for something moderately priced in midtown.

<Author>Tinytoons
<Content>Great hotel to stay in NYC Myself and my husband have just returned from a wonderful 5 night stay at the New York Helmsley Hotel. Location is excellent, only a 10 min walk to Times Square or a $5-$6 cab ride. From the moment we arrived at the hotel from the door staff (especially Ritchie) and bell boys to the reception desk staff all were fantastic and couldnt do enough for us. We had emailed previously and asked for a room on a high floor. We couldn't have gotten any higher on their 41st floor with an amazing view of the Crysler Building and city lights. The room was a great size with a huge bed and great shower. The room was cleaned daily and was always very tidy when we came back from a day of sightseeing. We were never disturbed by any noise during the night. We had an evening flight home and when I asked for a late checkout, there was no problem at all and they even held onto our cases for us as we took a final stroll around the city. Harry's Bar is small and a bit pricey, but hey it is a hotel after all! The only gripe I have about the bar was that it closed even when there were hotel guests still there drinking. I thought it would remain open until the last guest left???? We didnt eat in the hotel as we used the Pax Deli right next door which was perfect for brekkie. Security at night was appreciated as they checked that every guest had a room key to gain access to the lifts at night. We would highly recommend this hotel as a great base in the city.

<Author>tlemus
<Content>Great Experience Our stay at the New York Helmsley was extremely enjoyable. After exiting LGA, we only had a very short cab ride $20 + tip. We were taken to our room with a wonderful view of the Chrysler building, which was requested after letting them know by email that it was our anniversary. We stayed there 6 days, and its location (which was one of the primary reasons we chose to reserve in the first place) proved to be a major asset. We were very close to Union Station, and from there we were able to take the subway to all the major points of the city. It was clean and tidy, and an oasis after having spent a whole day walking. We were not expecting a 4 star hotel, and so we were not upset by what was missing. However, since our expectations weren high, we were pleasantly surprised by how much we got for the price we paid. The bar had the worst music ever, and the waitresses weren friendly or efficient. I think they rely on guests stopping for a drink, and so they take you for granted. Therefore, we just had a drink, we paid, and left the minimal tip.Other than that, we will definitely be back, and will definitely recommend it to all our friends.

Although convenient to the trains, this place is going down hill fast. For the price I paid (over $350.00 corporate rate) I would NEVER stay here again. On the upside, the elevator security guard was very personable - he was the only one. The bartender acted like it was an inconvenience for him to make you a drink to take to your room (way over priced!!!! by the way). I am very unhappy and let my company (a major insurance company) aware of the unsatisfactory accomodations.

<Author>Cohen_Jack
<Content>Good bet for the money My wife and I stayed at the New York Helmsley last Saturday evening to enjoy a night on the town without the commute back to the suburbs. For $358 including tax, we booked a room with a king size bed, which was not available on check-in. The clerk gave us a room with two doubles instead on a high floor with a nice view of the East River and the Verazzano Bridge in the background. The rooms are average size for a midtown New York hotel, with most, but not all, of the usual amenities. There is no fitness club on premises, no swimming pool, and the elevators are always crowded.The shower needed a little tinkering to get to work properly.On the plus side, the beds are comfortable, the staff is pleasant, the walls are thick, and the HVAC seemed to work. The hotel is in a great location-- 42nd Street, near Third Avenue. We had dinner at the Oyster Bar at Grand Central Station, one of the best seafood joints in New York for the money. After the theatre, we came back to our hotel and had a drink at Patrick Conway's, a great Irish pub near the train station. We forsook the $24 per person brunch at the hotel (which looked good), took a walk, and found the Townhouse Coffee Shop on Second Avenue and 38th Street, where for $25 for the two of us, we had a delicious breakfast. We walked over to First Avenue, where we viewed the United Nations and its gardens. By the time we left for home, we both thought we had the weekend experience we needed. I wouldn't necessarly rush back to the Helmsley for a similar expeience, but would come back there without undue worry or concern.

<Author>Ohjustpeachy
<Content>Good Location, Good Hotel Arrived at the hotel with pal, exhausted  looking forward to taking a much-needed nap but the smoking room booked wasn't ready. Apparently there's only one floor of smoking room in the whole hotel. We were earlier than the check-in time so had a couple of cocktails at Harry's Bar, where the 15% gratuity is added automatically! Returned to check-in a couple of hours later but still no smoking room ready so we accepted a non-smoking room instead and were assured it was a nice city view room - it was on the 30th floor, we could see the Chrysler and were delighted to find we had two beds instead of one to share. The hotel's staff were always very helpful and the bar was friendly. The beds were extremely comfortable and the in-room safe was a plus. Pax Deli next door to the hotel is ok for breakfast but if you walk up to the Pershing Sq Cafe (less than 5 mins, same side of road) they do a fabulous breakfast and it has a great atmosphere. The Capital Grille just a couple of mins up the road on the other side does a really nice dinner; it's not cheap but the staff are attentive and it's a pleasant treat. In the other direction is McFadden's Bar which serves some lovely fish dishes. You should have a cocktail at The View bar in the Mariott on Times Square, the views really are great  if you go for the sunset it's really quite pretty. Overall the hotel's location is great with Times Sq about 15 min walk and 5th Ave shopping a bit less. We thought Macy's was ok but Bloomingdales was the prettiest and brightest department store and Century 21 is worth a visit for past-season designer goods but is fairly chaotic.

<Author>dustie_rocks
<Content>Nice clean hotel We stayed in this hotel for 5 nights at the end of March. We had a room with two double beds (there were 3 family members staying in the room). We booked with a prepay website and got a very good deal. On arrival the reception area is very nice. We had no complaint with the hotel, the rooms were average size and very clean. The bathroom was large, lots of nice large bath towels and cleaned daily. There was no tea/coffee making facilities in the room but I often went to the deli next door and brought the drinks back. I had checked with Trip Advisor before travelling and had seen Pax deli recommended.. however it is really busy at rush hour in the mornings so the first morning we had breakfast in the hotel. We got the buffet breakfast.. It was 24 dollars but for that you got an amazing breakfast.. fresh tropical fruit, cereal, youghurt, crossaints, crusty rolls, doghnuts, waffles, french toast, bacon, sauage, etc etc. The juice was freshly squeezed and they refilled your glass as many times as you wanted. It was a really good meal and we didnt eat again until that night so it was worth the money. The location of the hotel is very good.. as we were mainly on a shopping/sightseeing trip it was perfect and very close to Grand Central station for easy access to a number of subway lines. We had a very good stay and I would highly recommend this hotel for a good stay in New York. Would stay in the hotel again.

<Author>findersmom
<Content>The Perfect Location! Stayed here while my son interviewed at Seton Hall University. Got a great deal on Expedia at $179/night for a Sat/Sun. The hotel is only 2 blocks from Grand Central Station. It's an easy walk there and we took the subway to everything--World Trade Center site, Times Square, Chinatown, Little Italy, Greenwich Village, SoHo, etc. To get to Seton Hall, we took the Subway to Penn Station, got tickets on the NJ Transit which took us straight to South Orange. The university was only a 10-minute walk from the train station.The hotel was very clean, great fluffy towels, comfortable beds, flat screen TV, free internet access. I travel frequently and am known as a hotel snob and I will definitely stay here again. The staff was soooo friendly, from check-in to check-out. They let us check in at noon, and allowed us late check out at 1:00. Every staff member was friendly and helpful. The room didn't have a coffee maker, which is not important to me because I don't drink coffee, however that may be an issue for some. But there's a Starbucks a half-block away and a Pax restaurant right next door. Also the room had no air-conditioning control, but we just opened our windows and it was comfortable. (That could be a problem during the summer months.)There's a great deli about 4 blocks down 2nd Ave. called Sarge's that's open 24 hours. Had wonderful BIG sandwiches and soup. Also convenient to the hotel is a CVS directly across the street that's open 24/7.Overall, we loved the location and hotel and will definitely stay here again.

<Author>mnendick
<Content>Basic but ok We were looking for a hotel to stay one night to see a show - so location was significant as we were arriving at Grand Central. All in all - for the price, this hotel was fine. We wanted to do little more than drop out bags, clean up, see the show, and then sleep. It was clean, relatively quiet, and near grand central. The staff seemed pleasant - particularly the guys dealing with the cars. Yes, its dated in almost every way in terms of decor, carpet etc., but as I said, it was clean and adequate for the price - which we paid 255. No coffee in room, no mini bar (which is fine because those are a rip off usually). There was a nice little place you could get coffee etc. right next to the hotel which worked out as a substitute. As to price, All the rest were upwards of 350 and up. So, it was a reasonable compromise. If I was staying longer and wanted to use hotel amenities, I might try something else.

<Author>anniefNorth
<Content>5 Nights at the New York Helmsley We arrived on 22nd Feb (we were there for our 25th Wed Anniversary on the 24th, ...a treat to ourselves) After a very long day we arrived at the Helmsley only to be told they were expecting us on the 27th, the receptionist made a phone call and told us it wasn't a problem etc etc and that they'd give us a nice room. The room was on the 14th floor, king sized bed, which was the best bed I've EVER slept in! The room was clean spacious enough for the two of us. We had a view of the chrylser building. My only disappointment was that they don't have any tea making facilities, although we later found out we could ask for them (and have it added to our bill) anyway... please take a credit card as you need it to check in with, not a debit card, one of ours wouldnt work but thank god my hubby has his american express which was accepted everywhere we used it. His goldfish card wasn't, nor was my personal bank card (which had plenty funds in it).. also beware of the cash machine in the lobby, it accepted my bankers card but never gave me any cash.. sorry to harp on about cash etc but if you're new to the states like we were, we didnt have a clue what would or wouldnt be accepted.Breakfast in Mindys (downstairs) was great, we founed we didnt need to eat again until about 4pm as the breakfast were buffet style so we ate as much as we wanted/needed.The staff in Minday and Harry's bar were very attentive, and being British we weren't used to it, but to be fair I could get used to it, the service was great, fast and efficient.The hotel is in a great situation for Grand Central, but to be honest we walked most of the time, we did buy a 7day metro ticket for $23 each which was so handy and if you're tired it's so easy just to jump on a train, having said that, cabs are cheap enough if you want to use them.Overall we had a fab time, and the hotel was as I expected, it was clean and comfy, and believe me, Im a clean freak and I was very happy to stay there.

<Content>Great Location, Great Staff I was a little uncertain about the hotel, as, from the pictures, it seemed a little dated. But it was great. From the moment we checked in, until we left, the staff were friendly, extraordinarily helpful and very professional.I was impressed by how many staff are around the hotel, always ready to help and be of service.The room was great. The location was excellent, as it was very close to the 4, 5, 6 subway lines (1.5 blocks to walk). There was a nice cafe downstairs (PAX), where you could get a good breakfast, sandwiches, baked goods to eat in or take away. I would absolutely stay at this hotel again, as it was a very positive experience.

<Author>Pets75
<Content>Great Stay at the Helmsley Just returned from a 4 night stay at the Helmsley and had a great stay with this hotel. I had some concerns before we left due to a few negative reviews but I need not have worried.We arrived late afternoon on Thursday and were greeted by friendly doorstaff and equally friendly check-in staff. There were a number of guests checking in and out but as soon as we walked in a new desk was opened for us.I had mailed the very helpful reservations manager before we travelled (and also Mark the hotel manager) and as they had told me they had made a note on my reservation of a request for a king room on high floor with view of Chrysler building - and that was what I got! I in fact had a choice of which floor I wanted. We stayed in room 3107 which had a king bed and looked just like the 'city room' on the website. Room was cleaned daily to good standard and we found part from one early morning when I was woken by a baby crying for an hour or so it to be very quiet. The room was a little stuffy and despite it being about 24 degrees we had the window open a few times for some fresh air, we did try using the controls for the heater/aircon but it only seemed to throw out hot air - this could well have been my lack of skills in operating this though! ;-)We did not use any of the bars of restaurants so can't comment here, we used PAX next door for coffees and snacks but were not impressed by their breakfasts - sorry majority of reviews! We preferred the Comfort Diner on E45th Street - yum and HUGE portions with friendly staff; I am missing the banana pancakes already!Overall our stay was great and the Helmsley was in an excellent location (about 3 minutes to Grand Central) and we paid a great price for the hotel.The checkout staff were equally as helpful and we have to say the doormen were great. The Bell Captain never seemed to stop and the doorman were always very friendly and helpful.If we return to NY - which I think we will (but maybe when it is slightly warmer and there is no snow-storm!) I would definitely check out staying at the Helmsley again and would happily recommend this to friends - in fact I already have!!P

<Author>Pneuma1
<Content>First class New York Helmsley Experience We have just returned from our first visit to New York and it was really terrific. We stayed at the New York Helmsley between 13 - 15 February and had a great stay there. The hotel was centrally located in mid town Manhattan close to all amenities.. Beautiful Central Station is very close as is Times Square. We found the reception staff very friendly and helpful and check in took no time at all. We were escorted to our room on 26th Floor by Anthony, one of the bellboys. He has been with the hotel a long time and was full of interesting info about NY. The Concierge was also very helpful providing maps and umbrellas when required. One point to be aware of is that you will be asked to secure a deposit of $100 for each night of your stay, either cash or card. Our travel agent had not mentioned this but we had picked it up from other reviews about this hotel. The hotel room was very well maintained with all mod cons, including LCD TV, recreational dressing gown and huge fluffy towels and was really warm, which was great as outside was so cold. Rooms were cleaned daily and left in mint condition. There are no tea/coffee making facilities but there is a great diner next door called PAX which is open from 6am - 10pm each day. Another good diner, is located in Pershing Square, try their Eggs Benedict, they are great!!!! All in all a very good stay in a highly recommended hotel. We will certainly be back.

As we are both smokers we requested a smoking room and were given room 2709. Wow!!! The room had two big beds with a 32 lcd tv with plenty of channels to chose from, the bathroom was marble with a hairdryer and plenty of large bathtowels, hand towels and face cloths. My highlight was that we had a superb view of the Chrysler Building across the street. <Author>sh3z
<Content>Great hotel, amazing view..minor setbacks We had a fantastic time at this hotel. I took my mum to NY, and I'm glad I chose so well! Yes, it's pricey...most hotels in the city are. Great, friendly service (I read the reviews here and was worried about that), a nice, clean spacious room and an AMAZING VIEW (see pics). We were on the 38th floor, and the only problem we had was that the lock on our door was dodgy..it took at least 6 tries to get the door open, and after getting someone to come and 'fix' it, nothing changed. Tiny problem in the long run though. Oh, and you have to request a fridge, which we did but never received anything. We ended up buying lots of water at the nearest store and stocking it in our room. The location is unbeatable - smack in the middle of everything. Go outside, look up- Chrysler building. A 2 minute walk to Grand Central, a quick walk or taxi/subway straight to the major avenues and Times Sq. Subway station is a minute or 2 away from the hotel, and there are plenty of Starbucks around to keep you going. In the other direction 5 minutes away is the UN building. We didn't eat at the hotel restaurant as it was so expensive, but we had a few Apple Martini's and mini-cheeseburgers at the bar (both delicious!). There's a great place next door which serves excellent, cheap food for a quick breakfast or lunch- so do that instead. All in all, we had a wonderful first trip to NY, and it was nice to have this hotel to come back to at the end of those exhausting days. A tip - e-mail the hotel a night or two before you arrive, and request a room on an upper floor with a view of the Empire State. I e-mailed and explained it was our first time, we were really excited and would love it if they could help - which they did. I miss sitting on the window ledge at sunrise and staring at that view :)

Of course we had to do a Broadway show and saw the Phantom of the Opera - marvellous. The Christmas tree at Rockefella Centre is magical and the Centre is worth a visit. <Author>Ramsden85
<Content>First time in New York After returning from a 5 night stay at The New York Helmsley from January 10th 2008, I have to admit I was very happy. If it is your first time to New York, the hotel may seem daunting at first, but believe me it is fabulous! All staff, no matter if they be catering assistants, receptionists, room maids, or security are fun and easy going. The hotels breakfast wasnt really fantastic to what we wanted, so we used the deli located just next door; try option 3, I loved it! Mindys restaurant is superb food, but maybe a little pricey; the cheaper alternative is to use Harrys Bar on the ground floor, in which case I reccomend the Sirloin Burger with Chedder  Bacon!The Helmsley is located directly in the center of most of the attractions you will probably want to visit whilst in New York. No more than 10 minutes in a taxi to either Bloomingdales or Macys (Opposite directions), and the Empire State Building, and a simple stroll left and up through 42nd street to Times Square and Grand Central Station. Do visit Bryan Park, just before Times Square, walking distance from the hotel. It has a lovely outside iceskating area, which I considered much better than the one in central park!

<Author>eurospender
<Content>Great value for Manhattan Our first long visit to NY (7 days over Xmas. Family of four - 2 grown up kids 22 .19. Wanted a mid priced but comfortable hotel relatively close to NY attractions. WIth so many available it was difficult to know best to be special for our visit over Christmas.On arrival at JFK, had booked Supershuttle service in advance via expedia. This proved excellent - a courtesy phone next to info desk at arrival hall got service within 20 mins.Other option can be yellow cab which charges $45 flat rate from JFK to any manhattan hotel ( but metered on return journey) Also discovered bus service stops 1 block from hotel.Hadnt really realised how good location of hotel was. First wonder was that iconic Chrysler building was the first thing you saw outside the hotel as you looked skyward. Awesome ! Impressive drivein/out front entrance and large lobby giving a feeling of above average class. Reception and lobby crew friendly. A major plus is 6 lifts ensuring little waiting time. We were on 14th floor, unfortunately with only a view of the office block opposite but the room was clean, two excellent good size double beds ( yes the kids had to share ! ) clean bathroom/shower and was quickly made our base. As other travellers have mentioned, a silly let down which did niggle us each morning was the lack of any drink making facilities. Although room service was available, it just seemed a bit pricey, certainly on a daily basis. However, this was made up for ( again as mentioned by others ) with the excellent Pax deli next door which became the main breakfast ritual ( total about $6 a head for large (their medium)coffee and egg/sausage/bacon muffin. To spoil yourself, a visit to Pershing Square opposite Grand Central Station ( 1 block away - 5 mins) offered a great breakfast treat $92 for total blowout. Transport for us becameeither simply walking - we walked miles - but for some reason it didnt seem bad. Times Square, the heart of it all was only 15 mins away ( enough to walk off breakfast )or taxis. As we were 4, it was actually the most economic and convenient way of getting around - except at peak times e.g. 6pm ish or 8pm ish. Getting to theatres trhough Times Square was gridlock - so allow time.But Helmsley to Times Square was on average $6-$8 including tip usually expected but gratefully received.Restaurants abound with huge variation of price. Most add on 15% gratuity and even on till receipt suggest more but its up to you. Best value 1 block down from Times Square we found was a Chinese Eat as Much as you like called Mid Town Buffet on 7th Ave. AT lunchtime it was $7.95 and this INCLUDED bottomless Coke/Sprite. Silly value. In the evening it went up to $11.95. Needless to say we ate there twice. Have never seen so many King prawns in my life ! An absolute must. Other recommends are TGI Fridays on Times Square and Lindys and if you are into prawns then a MUST visit is to Bubba Gump in Times Square too- atmosphere and amazing food ( quantity too ) something not to miss.We are theatre people so Broadway was a must and no let downs here. Try and book direct with box office. The premium seat prices are well over the top. For those on the cheap, visit the discount ticket stall just off times square on the day of a show. You might be lucky. A must for us was the radio city christmas spectacular. Glitzy, glam and the famous rockettes. A christmas special. The theatre itself is a wonder - would imagine the backstage visit would be worthwhile.Attractions - we took a helicopter trip as a special ($170 for 12 mins) , rockafella centre top of the rock definitely for a view of the skyline ( Had already done empire state last time) and the very poignant ground zero visit. We did staten island ferry ( passing but not stopping at liberty island) via a 5 hour tour by new york party tours - seemed a good deal with a smaller bus size and definitiely dedicated guide ($60).There is just so much to see and do. We crammed all we could into our week and christmas made it very special - definitely a time of year to visit. And the Helmsley is certainly a based to return to. Thanx to all there for making our 2007 stay in the Big Apple so memorable.

<Author>cmalloy
<Content>My last review still stands My second review of the New York Helmsley is almost identical to my first, which was written last year. The staff is still helpful and courteous, the location remains great, and the price is right. Ironically, my shower was not the best (like last year's). The water poured equally from the showerhead and the tub's spigot. Additionally, the room's cleanliness was a little lacking; there were a couple of hairs in the tub. And at the risk of being overly critical, there was a need for touch up paint on the doors, but the rest of the room was fine. The rooms are good-sized for NY's primo area and all in all, I remain very satisfied with my experience. The price of $200.00 a night for this area is hard to beat. We still noticed that the rooms were a bit overheated, just open the window and the stuffiness is forgotten. I hesitate to recommend that remedy because of environmental concerns. Again, these problems are minor if you get a good price. Oh, one positive is security: in the evening, the hotel security checks room keys before allowing patrons to go to their rooms

<Author>charmedalt
<Content>Perfect place to stay in NYC This hotel is fabulous! I read many of the reviews AFTER I booked this hotel and I have no regrets. True, there is no coffee in the room but room service will bring you a pot of good coffee for 5.95. The staff is amazing and the location couldn't be any better. My husband and I went here for our one year anniversary and now want to make it a yearly tradition with our whole family. The location is perfect-you have easy access to everything. We only took a cab once and that was to the airport (LGA). I would recommend as a tourist to get the Greyline 3 day hop on hop off pass. It is well worth the $ (112.00/per person). Note that the museums are donation only but they will ask for a certain amount-if you aren't planning on making a day of it, I would suggest maybe 10.00 rather than the 20.00 asked for. They will accept that, in fact will ask if 20.00 is okay. The people are incredible. I was apprehensive to go because of the past reputation of the city but it is now one of the safest cities in the world-I believe it! It is winter time and I am a clothes horse but if you want to see the city, do what I did and bring a few pair of jeans, some warm sweaters (winter time) and most importantly, very comfortable shoes. We walked miles and miles-I wish I had brought a pedometer so I could gauge how far we walked. The hotel also has a pretty nice workout room as well. Our room was on the 29th floor-we did have somewhat of a view of the Chrysler building but the room was so nice it wasn't an issue. The only negative thing that I can say about the room is that the lighting is very dim-especially the bathroom lighting. If you want knock off purses, skip Canal Street and go to Ground Zero, there is where you find the nice knock offs but the sellers are pretty discrete. We got 5 for $140.00, 4 Coach and 1 Kate Spade, very nice ones. Enjoy your stay, the hotel is fabulous and the food is really good and the prices are comparable to most of the restaurants. Note that a 15% gratuity at most places is already added in to your total. Have a great time!!!

<Author>Amanda64
<Content>NYH - Great location, good value I was in a group of 7 visiting NYC for shopping and Christmas atmosphere, we stayed for 4 nights and couldn't really fault the hotel. Reception staff were very friendly and welcoming and the porters were always pleased to help with luggage and shopping. One porter quite happily escorted me to my room as I don't like using lifts on my own!! There is a fabulous deli. right next door for great breakfasts and snacks, and it is very well situated for subway and buses. The twin rooms were great, with comfortable beds and good sized bathrooms. The triple room requested was exactly the same as the twins, i.e. two double beds which meant 2 people sharing a bed, but from previous experience that is standard for NY hotels. A hairdryer is provided but no kettle. We were on the 19th floor overlooking 42nd Street so had a fantastic view of the Chrysler building and the rest of our party were on the 20th floor looking over 41st Street with a great view of the Empire State building so we really felt part of New York as soon as we arrived.

<Author>marysj
<Content>Very Pleased We just returned from the NYH and have to say that we were very pleased. I wanted a good location, cleanliness and I didn't want to break the bank. In the end, we went for the NYH and are very glad we did. The location is fantastic - you can walk to Times Square in under 15 minutes and the subway is less than a 5 minute walk. Our room was large, very clean and we had a view of the Chrysler Building if we stood in the right spot. Bathroom was spic and span with loads of hot water. We found the staff very accommodating and were glad to have a bar and restaurant in the building after one particularly long, cold day. Bar has a nice atmosphere and the martinis were pretty darn good. Good deli next door for breakfast - Pax. The only problem we had was that the room was hot, despite not having turned the heating on. Most of the time we had the windows open. That can be a bit noisy - even 34 floors up - but that's what NY is all about. Overall, would stay again and wouldn't hesitate to recommend it. Nice, large, good value hotel.

<Author>TW1
<Content>Good Hotel, Great Location When we arrived we were given a lovely room that we were very pleased with. We then went out for a few hours only to find on our return that we could not get in our room. When we told reception that we could not get the key card to work they informed us that someone else had our room and that they had moved all our baggage out of there into another room!. Unfortunatly they had left our passports and all our money in the old room with the new customers ! Not a good start. Although we did get everything back the management were not very appologetic. After this bad start things did get better, and I have to say that the rooms were very clean, as were the bathrooms. The hotel is also about 10-12 mins from times square, 4 mins from central station and about 15mins from The Empire State Building, so well situated. Harry's Bar in the hotel is a nice place for a drink and the Bar Tender (Orlando) is very friendly. Have breakfast in John's Diner up the road, as it is very 'New York Diner' ish, and also a lot cheaper than the hotel. The staff on reception were generally very helpful, and the view from our floor (29th) of the Chrysler building and street below was 'awesome'!. Although we had initial problems We would stay here again. Don't forget to visit Ground Zero as it is very moving.

<Author>WorthingTraveller
<Content>No fault found We have just returned from our first trip to the Big Apple. Chose this hotel after hours of trawling through Trip Advisor and it didn't let us down. The staff were friendly, welcoming and polite and the room was clean, comfortable and quiet. We had upgraded to the Premier room and felt it was worth it for the extra bit of space it gave. The only downside was the price of the drinks in Harry's bar, which came as a bit of a shock. Experience taught us, though, that spirits always seem to come as a double measure in NY and with a price that more than matches, so it seems a bit unfair to hold it as a minus against the hotel.Also, although it was right on top of the Chrysler Building and not far from Grand Central Station, It was a little bit away from the majority of the main attractions, which meant extra walking. This didn't bother us but is something to take into account if mobility is a problem.

<Author>Happy_Parsnips
<Content>Great position Helpful staff especially consierge. Grumpiest male deputy manager I'veever met but he was the only unhappy one there. Food just average but next door there is a `Pax' that you can get breakfast to eat in or take back to room which is very reasonable. No refreshment tray in room so you might want to take a travel kettle etc. with you if you like a drink first thing. Old hotel but fine, rooms larger than a lot in town and bathroom old but fine and clean. You can walk everywhere from this hotel, or the doorman can easily whistle up a taxi for you and these are really reasonably priced. Remember to ask for a high room to get a good view. Pier 17 area down near wall street definatelyworth a visit, lovely views, nice little shopping center and good barsplus short walk from the helicopter trip place which I would recommenddoing for sure if the weather is good (book through hotel consierge) plus its a 10 minute walk from World Trade Centre site if you want to visit. St. Pauls chapel opposite WTC definately one to visit - very moving. Regarding shopping watch out for the independent electrical retailers who all seem to advertise cheap offers in the window on cameras, apple ipods etc., that don't materialise in the shop. Best stick to the tried and tested big shops or radio shack for gadgets. Very easy to blow an absolute fortune on not very much so watch out. Remember to add approx. 10% sales tax to everything you see and also that restaurants suggest up to 20% of bill as gratuity which can bump it up (there is sales tax on this as well). Would definately stay hereagain.

<Author>traveluvr
<Content>Nice hotel, a bit 'tired' The New York Helmsley is a very nice hotel in a great location - very near Grand Central so you can access both trains and the Subway very easily. With just a few blocks walk to Time Square, there is plenty of shopping and restaurants to be visited. We spent 3 days at the hotel and they did 'upgrade' us to a 'room with a view' on the 37th floor, but that meant going from a king size bed to a room with 2 double beds - but the view was worth it. The floor was quiet so no complaints there. The room itself was nicely decorated but quite 'tired' looking. A re-decoration would have allowed us to give it a much higher rating. The room did have a large flat screen TV and in room safe. The bathroom was small but adequate - wallpaper was peeling at the seams, vanity mirror was dropped in the frame. They did have free WIFI internet available in the rooms however, we did have issues getting logged in - actually had to use another guest details to do so (per the front desk)! Perhaps we are being a bit fussy, but the price of this hotel is not cheap and we feel that for the cost of the room, they should be top-notch; but then again, this is NYC and nothing is really inexpensive there. I think they should at least have had coffee/tea facilities in the room. All in all, it served our purpose but I don't think we will be staying there on our next visit to NYC - there are just too many other hotels to try there.  
<Date>Oct 28, 2007

<Author>gottogonow
<Content>Great Central Location We stayed at the hotel for 3 nights (Oct. 3 - 6th. ) before starting a cruise.The hotel was in a great location, near Grand Central Station and the Chrysler building. We asked for one of the renovated rooms in the upper levels but none were available, we were given a room on the 22nd floor. The next morning the front desk called us and told us they had one of the upper rooms available and offered to move us. I felt their followup was beyond the call. Very professional and appreciated, however we declined as I felt we were high enough. My only complaint about the room was that there was no coffee maker, refrigerator or bottled water available. We also had the misfortune of being awaken at 3:00 am by the hotel's fire alarms going off and the fire engines arriving 22 floors below our window. We gathered in the hall along with the rest of the guests on our floor to plan our escape down the staircase. After repeated unanswered calls to the desk downstairs we started our escape. Finally a voice in broken English came across a public address system that it was a false alarm. I am disabled and walk with a cane. I would never have survived that 22 floor escape. We loved New York City and we would probably consider staying here again but next time on a lot lower floor!

<Author>Bruzzz
<Content>Absolutely Stunning Hotel We completed an Eastern Us tour and booked out of our tour hotel early. Arrived at the New York Helmsley 11.00 am which is early by US standards as rooms are only supposed to be vacated by 12.00noon.We were were very pleasantly surprised by the very friendly and helpful desk staff, who booked us into a room immediately without any extra charge. We were even able to choose a smoking room on floor reserved for smoking rooms. A lot of travellers really appreciate this comfort vz standing on the street corner having a quick puff.The room was a large double room on the 27th floor facing East 42nd Street. The room was clean, very well appointed, modern, it felt 5 starish, and the view was fantastic. Look to the left and see Chrysler building in all it's glory, and to the right you can see the United Nations building.The bathroom was also very modern, clean, lots of towels, shampoos, soaps etc. and also had a small refrigerator which was fantastic.The Hotel is really classy for the price we paid, very close to many of the main sight seeing attractions which is perfect when you are on a sight seeing mission as we were.We were out for the most of each day, but when we returned from our sightseeing, the rooms were made up and everything was just perfect.We unfortunately did not sample the hotel's food, as we were on the go, but grabbed breakfast next door at PAX or up 42nd at the Grand Central Food concourse where there must be more than 40 food outlets, with every type of food conceivable and at reasonable prices.Our compliments to the management and staff for being so polite and helpful. I will always go back to The New York Helmsley on East 42nd. I recommend this hotel to everybody who is looking for a really classy 3-4 star hotel. <Author>eoleary
<Content>Great location Just back from a five day family trip to NYC from Ireland. The NY Helmsey was just what I had hoped for. Well located, clean and friendly. We had a room on the twenty first floor with a brill view ( not that you are going to spend time looking out the window with so much to do and see). We did not eat at the hotel but instead had breakfast at 'Pax' next door (good value food and handy).We found a great place to eat in the evening (Libretto's on 3rd. Avenue). Out the hotel door and turn left. Left again on 3rd. Avenue and you will find it a seven minute walk away on the right of the avenue. Great atmosphere loads of good italian food and nice wine at a good price. Family loved it. Wo Hop on Mott Street in China Town was another good experience for a family meal. This chinese 'cafe' in the basement is busey as it is well used by newyorkers (which is why we tried it after seeing the natives going in).If your stuck for time (as we were one evening when going to a show) a nice way of having fast food can be found at a no frills outlet just past and next door to McDonalds on the left past Grand Central (up the 42nd.street from the hotel). Here you can have a pizza or pasta dish made up to your own preference while you watch. You then sit down and eat it piping hot out of a plastic bowl with plastic knife and fork and a bottle of soda or water.Tip for the trip would be as we did. Go up Rockerfeller Centre in the morning and the Empire State in the evening (we went up at 11pm and found the ques to be very short).We found that newyorkers in general were either very rude or very nice and rather than get annoyed, we let there be a competion to find the rudest and the nicest. We felt very safe anywhere we went and can't wait to go back (in which case we will head for the NY Helmsley again).

<Author>pakia9
<Content>Belligerent security staff, bad atmosphere We stayed here recently. Hotel is well located in midtown Manhattan near to the Chrysler building and Grand Central. Rooms were clean and ours had a nice view of the Empire State Building. There is a heavy (and heavy handed) security presence in the hotel - most notably in the lobby. Our 6 year old accidentally locked the bathroom door (thankfully from the outside) and we couldn't open it. I rang the front desk and who did they send up to fix it? a security guard in shades! Mind you he did manage to get it open and was on the walkie talkie to the maintenance guys to 'DISREGARD - I REPEAT DISREGARD!! We laughed ourselves silly when he left.Another night I was in the bar having a drink and just about to return to my room. I was immediately stopped by a BIG security guy who loudly questioned me in front of everyone. He wanted to see my room card and when I pointed out I did not have it with mehe began eyeballing me and posturing aggressively. I honestly thought he was going to throw me out there and then. I told him my room number and he let me go, sneering at me as I hurriedly left the scene. What annoyed me about this was that all he had to do was ask me my name and room number and check it with the front desk - instead he seemed more intent on intimidating and humiliating me (he succeeded on both counts). And I could have given him any old baloney by just giving my room number! I did ring the manager to complain. She said she would meet with department heads to discuss the matter. I wasn't at all surprised to hear nothing more. The only time we felt threatened at all during our stay in New York was when we were in this hotel. We'll definitely visit NY again but we'll be giving this place a wide berth.

Then he had a problem with the fact we had no US money yet to give him a tip (for a job badly done mind you) so he stormed out slamming our door. Welcome to NYC! These two incidents put a horrible start to our trip - all thanks to the pathetic staff and service at the Helmsley. We had to have our bank refuse the second payment and finally they found our booking - with no apolagies just a bad attitude.The only saving grace - the hotel was nice and the location was perfect.

<Author>SavvyUrbanite
<Content>Great value New York is extremely expensive during the week. It is hard to find a decent hotel for less than $300 a night. This is one of the few, if only, first-class hotel that offers such a rate in the dense midtown area. If you are willing to spend $500+ a night elsewhere, be my guest and best of luck to you.After reading some of the nightmarish reviews I was a bit apprehensive. I booked directly with the hotel and was given a fine room on the 23rd floor. This may be the way to go to guarantee one of the refurbished rooms on the higher floors. If you hate street noise, ask for a room on the back street side. 42nd Street traffic at 6 am is pretty loud. Bathroom a good size and clean. Beds fine.Our corner room was superb, with view of Chrysler building.Breakfast a good value in nice dining room.As I said, if you are looking for value, book here. I have heard that if you get a room through the cut-rate Internet sites you might not get the best room. But then you might if you play your cards right when you arrive.Cheers.
