<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location... We have just returned from a 5 night stay at the New York Helmsley and we thought it was great...after reading some comments we were a little apprehensive ..but our fears were unfounded when we went into our room...it was on the 29th floor newly renovated with stunning views of the Chrysler Building going down towards Grand Central Station...the room was spotless and the bed was so comfortable (one of the best we have had in a hotel) and it was huge.. <Author>AndieF
<Content>Overall a good experience made better by a wonderful staff I just got back from a one-night stay at the NY Helmsley. We initially got off to a bad start at the hotel. I'd asked for a room on one of the upper floors, only to be booked on the 9th floor. The front desk was very accommodating, moving us to a different location -- on the 33rd floor. I want to personally commend Lily and the others at the front desk for being professional, courteous, and for going above and beyond to ensure our stay was a good one. The room itself was a decent size, and the view was magnificent-- the skyline and even a glimpse of the river. The room was very clean, and while we appreciated the small, flat-screen TV, it was odd to have an empty armoire still in the room where I imagine the previous tv had been housed. Our only complaint about the room was very dim lighting in the bathroom. It cast everything in a sort of grey tinge. The location is fairly convenient, though the neighborhood is quiet at night. We actually walked across town to the theatre district -- which took about 20 to 25 minutes. We didn't eat at the hotel, so I can't comment on their restaurant. In all, I felt this was a fairly good experience...made so much more enjoyable by the professional and accommodating staff.

<Author>Nikki79
<Content>Dirty Bed Linen I booked this hotel as I was treating my mother and two sisters to a trip of a lifetime to New York city for 3 nights from the 3rd May. I checked out the reviews here on tripadvisor and thought it looked a safe enough bet. We were planning on being out shopping and sightseeing all day long so all we really wanted was a clean bed and bathroom - nothing fancy. However, we didnt receive this.....On the first night my mother got into her bed and found a long black hair beside her which obviously didnt belong to her and when she pulled back the covers the sheets were stained with blood and had hairs all over them from a previous occupant. The sheets hadnt been changed from the previous guests, instead the housekeeper had simply remade the beds with soiled linen. My aunts bed appeared to be stained with urine or something else equally unsavoury. This is just not acceptable in a supposed 4 star hotel. The most basic function of a hotel is to provide a clean bed to sleep in and for over EURO 230 a night it isnt too much to expect. I simply cannot express how disgusted I am at the lack of hygiene displayed and the complete lack of pride the staff/hotel owers have in their establishment. I wouldnt invite someone into my home and ask them to sleep in soiled sheets let alone expect someone to pay for the privilege! I have been in hostels that were cleaner than this room. In the second room which my sisters and I shared there was blood stains on the carpet and the mattress bases were heavily stained but at least our sheets were clean. The rooms are badly worn and in serious need of redecorating. We were staying on the 19th floor and these are the old unrenovated rooms. After reading the reviews here it would appear that the renovated rooms are far superior to the tatty lower floors which really are not suitable to be let out.When we complained to the on-duty manager about the condition of the rooms all he could do was apologise but said that as I had paid upfront he couldnt compensate us for the stomach churning incident. I filled in a customer comment card and both my aunt and mother wrote letters to the general managers outlining how awful the rooms were but we have not heard anything back as yet. It is only 48 hours later but with something as serious as this I would have expected an immediate response.The location of this hotel is really excellent and some of the staff were very friendly and the food in the restaurant was great ( we ate there the first night before the soiled sheets incident) however this is all overshadowed by the dirt of the rooms. If a hotel cannot provide its patrons with a clean bed what else is it lacking? My advise is DO NOT STAY HERE unless you're guaranteed one of the renovated rooms! It really is a shame because this could be a great hotel but it fell well short of my expectations.

<Content>Leona Would Not Approve For the significant cost (approx. $300/night) and the location, I expected a hotel that was well-lit, clean, with up-to-date furnishings and details, and with a staff (e.g., front door, restaurant, etc) that was readily available and service oriented. <Author>Notoverlyfussy...
<Content>Everything you need and more This is a very impressive hotel and my wife and I stayed here as part of our honeymoon. Having read the reviews here, we were happy enough that the comments were mostly positive. The location on 42nd St is ideal as a base for shopping/sightseeing/activities. We spent 4 nights here starting on St. Patricks day and during this time we shopped in Macy's, the Manhattan Mall and Jersey Gardens, We went to a game in the Garden and did a helicopter tour of Manhattan. With the exception of the helicopter trip, everything was within walking distance.The rooms were big for a New York Hotel. a HD flat screen LCD TV in our room and a comfortable bed. The room was on the 32nd floor and looked across the city skyline to the Chrysler building. Importantly the room was clean. The bar in the hotel was comfortable enough but to be fair, we were not in NY to see a hotel bar and only stopped off for a drink.We found the staff to be extremely helpful and courteous. I have seen some comments about the staff and I guess that it is just the luck of the draw. On Paddy's Day, the staff were all wering green flowers and I was chatting to the porter (Joe) about this and when we came back down to the lobby to go out, he was waiting with lapel flowers for my wife and I. A nice touch.The Pax deli is pretty nice but also walk down the street and opposite grand central, there is a lovely restaurant that serves great breakfast. They advertise it as the best in the world... I must say, it is pretty good!For a non-expensive activity, try Central Park. There is an Ice rink in the centre and some great views of the city. We walked back to the Helmsley from Central Park via 5th Avenue and visited St Patricks Cathedral. One regret was not going to the 'Top of the rock' but that is a must for next time. Locals tell us that the views are better than the Empire State Building.For nightime activities, there is no shortage but behind Grand Central station on 43rd btwn Madison  Vanderbilt you will find Annie Moores Irish pub. We didn't try the food but the beer and service was pretty good. If you do go shopping, there is a shop in the Manhattan mall that I particularly enjoyed. It's called Brookstone and is full of gadgets and gizmos as well as having massage chairs. Great place to spend an hour while the wife goes shopping! Also, bring your passport to Macy's. There is an office upstairs where they will give you an 11% discount card for all purchases.The outlet stores are full of good deals and we opted for the Jersey Mall as it was 30mins on a bus from Port Authority and $10 return on the bus versus $38 and 90mins to woodbury Common. Again, bring the passport for a discount card. Great hotel, great city.

<Author>Sapper123
<Content>So-So Helmsley Close to Grand Central Station, Times Square, and Lincoln Tunnel (in case you are coming-in via Newark International Airport). High definition television in our room was nice, but there was no complimentary coffee. Back in the 1980, this must have been a great hotel, but unfortunately, there appears to have been few renovations since that decade. <Author>WendyAM
<Content>Great stay at the Helmsley I booked the Helmsley through bedsearchers.com after reading all the reviews. I emailed them before we left to let them know we'd be arriving late and to ask for a non-smoking room and they emailed back to confirm everything. We arrived just after midnight and the hotel receptionist was friendly and check in was quick. Our room was a double double on the 39th floor - and our first morning we awoke to an amazing sunrise we saw out of the window over the east river. The bathroom was quite large with quality Soames  Gilchrist toiletries and lots of towels for the four of us. The room had a plasma tv with plenty of channels and the beds were comfortable. I was able to use the business centre computer to check in for our return flight on BA with no charge. Breakfast could be as huge or small as you wanted - although the guy who seemed to be in charge was a little dour, though all the others were friendly, as were the concierge, bell captain - in fact everyone. The location is a five minute walk from the United Nations building, about 15 mins max from Time Square, in the same street as the Grand Central Station and within easy walking distance of just about everywhere. All in all, we had a great stay here and would definitely go back.

<Author>RedJak
<Content>Great Hotel, excellent location We have just returned from a fabulous 5 night stay at the Helmsley to celebrate my 40th birthday. We found the staff to be very helpful and check in was efficient and quick. The rooms were spacious and adequate for our needs. The bar was nice and cosy and great for a drink at the end of a long day. The hotel is in an ideal position to all the major sights and the easiest way to see everything is to walk as the buildings are amazing! For breakfast we used PAX next door which offered a huge variety of food all day long. There is also a lovely Italian restaurant opposite the hotel. The hotel was situated close to Grand Central Station and within easy walking distance to the Empire State Building. We also visited the Rockerfeller Centre and went to the top, the views were just amazing and in our opinion far better than the view from the Empire State Building (we bought out tickets online before we travelled for both of these attractions which saved having to queue!) The hotel is within a 15-20 minute walk from Times Square, Central Park and fifth avenue! We would also highly recommend a helicopter trip - the only way to see New York - We cant wait to come back!

<Author>yerominas
<Content>Good Hotel, Great Location Stayed at this hotel Feb 07. Superb location on 42nd street between 2nd  3rd Avenues. Less than five minutes walk to Grand Central Station  not much further to Times Square etc. Good comfortable room with two double beds, table  armchairs, TV, lovely bathroom with good shower, ice machine on corridor. Very friendly staff. Ask for high floor room if possible for best views. We were floor 12  could see nearby beautiful Chrysler Building  UN HQ on a sideways view, but the higher the better. Didn't use bar or restaurant so can't comment. Useful business centre (small charge) in lobby with two PC's  printers - good for reconfirming flight. Fantastic cafe next door - Pax - with lovely fresh food for breakfast  through the day,  loads of other food places nearby. Don't miss Grand Central Station - beautiful building, fantastic fresh food market, nice shops,  great dining area downstairs - especially with kids as there's lots of different food stalls to choose from  plenty of places to sit. Loved New York  for those worried about safety (like I was) - don't, I never felt threatened or insecure even at night.

<Content>Fantastic Hotel - great location! The boyfriend  I arrived with Delta Airlines from London Gatwick on a Thursday for a 4 night stay - we were immediately impressed by the attentive  friendly staff at Check In - I would particularly like to thank Deirdre for her honest advice about where not to venture across town! The bathroom was nicely finished in marble  was clean. We had a great view of the Empire State Building  felt very faint looking down from our room onto the traffic below!! There was a great little cafe next door called Pax - I would recommend going there for brekkie as the hotel charges about $18 each!!The hotel's location was ideal - Times Square, 5th Ave etc were only about 15mins walk away, Grand Central was the next block along. We had a great meal out at The Peking Duck on E. 53rd Street, and also an expensive but yummy meal at the Sparks Steak House on E. 46th St - steaks  wine list very impressive!If you want to go ice skating in Central Park, keep in mind that the rink closes at 2.30pm on Mondays and Tuesdays! All in all, a wonderful birthday weekend.Just a couple of down points:1. Tipping - everyone expects a tip  it drove us mad!!! You're even expected to tip a barman for only pulling the top off a beer bottle.2. Caroline's Comedy Club - we felt like we got scammed here!It was rated 2nd in our guidebook, so thought we'd check it out on our last night. Tickets were $24.50  you had to purchase 2 drinks each. We bought 2 drinks at the bar before we entered the stage area, but were told afterwards that these drinks didn't count towards our quota! At about $13 each (for a beer!) these were ridiculously expensive! The comedy was awful, not really comedy at all, as the main act 'comedian' decided to get up and give everyone a sermon about 'loving thy neighbour' and how 'black brothers' should respect one another!! Not exactly our cup of tea!

<Content>Highly recommend the Helmsley Three of us stayed for a week at the Helmsley this month. Also the Comfort Diner on 45th St is great for breakfast. Also, this hotel seems to be very popular with airlines - we saw pilots and cabin crew from Alitalia and Virgin and some others staying there.I can't recommend this hotel enough and can't wait to return!

<Content>Fantastic hotel My sister and I have just got back from a five night stay at this hotel and we thought it was fantastic. We was a little worried as we had seen mixed reviews for thid hotel but I don't know how anyone could not have been impressed by this. As soon as we walked in we were greeted by the very friendly and helpful bell boy. The ladies behind the front desk were also very accomodating. We were shown up to our room that was amazing. Rooms were of very good size with three phones, iron and board, safe in the wardrobe tv and alarm clock. To say this was posh for us was an understatement. We paid a little exrta for what we had hoped as a lot of cheaper hotels seemed to have bad reviews. We are so glad we picked this hotel, it was gorgeous. We even had th taxi door opened and the door spun for us, we didn't have to lift a finger if we did't want. The location is great too. Just across form the Christler and down the road from grand central. Right at the heart of everything really. So if you're in doubt whether to book this or not, I strongly advise you do.

<Author>Ane
<Content>Great Hotel! Just returned from a 5 day stay at the Helmsley and couldn't be happier about the experience! From our super-fast check in process to our super-fast check out it was marvellous. I requested a room on a high floor - no problem. We were given a room on 34 with a great view of the Empire State Building. All of the staff, without exception, were courteous and helpful and did not 'hover' for tips. All requests were dealt with immediately and withut fuss (our toilet backed up and the maintainance guy was at the door in 3 minutes after I called reception). We didn't use the bar or restaurant (we prefer something more casual) but they looked great. The area where the hotel is situated is perfect - within walking distance of Times Square, Grand Central Station and the great shopping on 34th Street (including Macy's) and just far enough away from the hustle  bustle to ensure a relaxed stay. If I were to recommend a few things to do/see I'd say take the Circle Line 3 hour boat tour (from pier 83 at 42nd  12th), eat at Josie's Restaurant (at 38th  3rd), have a beer at O'Lunney's Bar (just off Times Square on 47th Street), go to Jersey Gardens for the shopping (111 bus from Port Authority Bus Terminal on 8th Avenue at 42nd Street), see the inside of Grand Central Station (a hop and a skip from the hotel), have breakfast at PAX Deli (next door to the hotel) and just have a great time in New York!

<Author>Wonderwoman0126
<Content>Great holiday stay Having researched many potential accommodations, we enjoyed a wonderful stay at the Helmsley for a 4-night holiday trip! Bernardo upgraded us to a king room on the 40th floor, the view from which my NYC newbie boyfriend loved. The room and bathroom were spotless and the king bed was incredibly comfortable. Closet and drawer space were ample. This hotel is very well sound insulated. We never heard a peep from another room or another floor, and there seemed to have been high occupancy.We had a problem with our in-room safe (not the hotel's fault), and the abundant, expert and professional security and maintenance staff took care of it very quickly - on Christmas day, no less.Front desk, concierge. security and bell staffs were all very friendly and helpful yet refused to accept well-deserved tip money. And, of course, the location is prime for subway, walking and sightseeing enthusiasts. We will undoubtedly stay here again.Only one thing to watch out for - it is very hot in the winter on the upper floors. Take lightweight clothing to wear while in your room and keep some air conditioning circulating. This was a very minor annoyance that we were able to deal with by keeping the room door ajar and windows open while awake. Overall we had a very comfortable and enjoyable stay. Kudos to the hardworking Helmsley staff!

<Content>Great hotel Great location Stopped at the New York Helmsley 4th december 2006 for 4 nights. Was a bit concerned about the rooms after looking at some of the reviews. The room was on the 21st floor it was lovely and warm and very big even with two doubles in. The bathroom was lovely thought the bath was a bit small but when i got in realised it was great and deep. I understand that they are doing some of the rooms up even though ours was fine it was a little bit tired but since i was out of the hotel for 12-14 hours all i wanted was a clean bed. The only down side is no tea and coffee making but i suppose you could bring your own. This wasn't too bad as there is a great deli next door the staff are great and there sandwiches and soups are great. The subways are very safe there are usually guards riding on the trains. If you decide to use them the ticket booth people are very good and will direct you in the right direction. We are booking for next December and i would have no hesitation in choosing the Helmsley.

<Author>kirkjshurey
<Content>Location, location, location! Stayed at the New York Helmsley with 3 friends for a two night break.Check-in staff were friendly but bell captain was not particularly helpful as we were unable to store our bags prior to the room being available, due to 'security measures' which meant we wasted valuable time sitting with our suitcases at the bar rather than sightseeing.The room was on the 18th floor, large, but slightly shabby, although not dirty, with views of the Chrysler Building and Second Ave. Street noise was not too loud and no noise heard at all from other rooms. Room lacked tea/coffee making facilities or a safe and although a fridge was located in the bathroom, it didn't work. Plenty of comfortable new towels and decent toiletries were provided and service was quick when we asked for additional items. The bed was comfortable and iron/board handy to have.The best thing about the hotel for us was its location, just diagonally across from the Chrysler Building and a couple of blocks from Grand Central Terminal, 5th Ave. and Times Square. We managed to get an exceptionally good airline rate due to friends working for VAA, but I would not have paid full rack-rate as the hotel was simply too shabby for anything more than a weekend break and would benefit from a complete refurbishment. I would recommend this hotel for a long weekend if you can obtain a good rate.

<Author>ndwhyte
<Content>The NY Helmsley - a top spot My wife and I travelled to New York along with our niece and had originally booked another hotel but having read the horrific reviews on this website we decided to change. We booked the NY Helmsley based purely on location. And I'm glad we did. Although just a little further from the shopping districts than our original hotel I actually thought it was in a much nicer area....still only a 10 minute walk from Times Square, close to 5th Ave shopping and 1 block from Grand Central Station which is well worth a visit.The room was relatively large, clean and had it's own safe. No fridge but there are ice machines on each floor with ice buckets in the room. Room service called each day and rooms were always left tidy and towels changed each day.Over all I was very impressed with the hotel and would not hesitate to stay again.Only a few very minor gripesWe had booked a Double Double Premium room (apparantly have Plasma screen tvs) and paid a little extra for this but on arrival we were just assigned a standard double room. I queried this at the desk and they had none of the premium rooms available for the night we arrived (strange considering I booked directly through the hotel website!). The room we'd been given was fine so once I ensured that the extra premium on the bill had been removed we decided not to complain any further.Our room was at the back of the hotel and had a view of nothing, if you want views of the Chrysler Building ask for a room at the front of the hotel (although it may be a bit noisier!Mindys Restaurant and Harrys Bar are *very* expensive, (as is the Pershing Square Deli at GCS - beware! Pax Deli next dooor is great for breakfast/snacks and the Phoenix Garden on 40th Street (2 blocks behind the hotel) is a *superb* chinese restaurant, low on decor, low on price but very high on taste!

<Content>Lovely hotel I read many mixed reviews prior to my trip so was unsure what to expect but I should not have feared as this is a lovely hotel and overall my experience was excellent.My room was on the 25th floor: it was large, the bed was huge and very comfortable, there was extra beding, bathrobes and ample towels available. I did not have a new room with plasma tv and internet but mine appeared to be recently decorated, the furniture served its purpose, was comfortable and everywhere was spotlessly clean. Decor was quite old/traditional so it may not be to everyones taste but I could find no fault. Checking in and out took less than 5minutes and I did not encounter any rude staff pushing for tips. Had room service a few times and food was lovely.I would stay here again as it was in an ideal location to experience Manhattan, 5minutes walk to the Chrysler Building, Grand Central and the United Nations, 10minutes walk to Times Sqaure and Broadway. The one thing this hotel is missing is tea/coffee making faclities in your room.

<Author>twiggy-and-gin
<Content>Fantastic Hotel Overall I recently spent a week at the New York Helmsley Hotel and had a fantastic time in the hotel and in New York.On arrival to the hotel the staff were very helpful and friendly. There's always someone around to give you some help and advice at all times of the day/night. Every member of staff we met were very friendly towards us.We stayed in a twin room on the 31st floor with a fantastic view over 42nd street and buildings beyond (see my photos). The room was well equipped with flat-screen TV, comfortable beds, clean linen and a fantastic en-suite bathroom with plenty of towels, etc every day.Security at the hotel is fantastic with extra-safe security at night. Mindy's restaurant has excellent staff but the food is slight pricey for what you get. Harry's bar has a nice friendly feel and is not too expensive compared to other bars/pubs in New York. But obviously there's plenty of alternatives near the hotel instead if you wish!Location-wise the hotel wins me over again. Fantastic shops such as Gap are literally a minute away. Times Square is about a 10 minute walk and everything else is nearby. The Crysler building is literally opposite the hotel and The Empire State building is quite close too. We also walked from the hotel to 5th avenue to do a bit of shopping. It was about a 20 minute walk but there's plenty to keep you occupied on the way. The subway is very close to the hotel too so basically every area in New York is close to you!Overall I would rate this hotel 9.5/10 - it really was a great stay. The only downside would be Mindy's restaurant, although we only had breakfast in there. If you're planning a stay at the New York Helmsley Hotel, you won't be disappointed!

<Author>DubLass
<Content>Great Hotel  Having read lots of mixed reviews on this hotel, I was very apprehensive and dreading the worst. I will admit that I am very fussy when deciding on a hotel and after doing alot of research I decided on the New York Helmsley, I wasn't disappointed.We arrived on 26 Oct 06 for 4 nights and checked in around 2pm. We had booked a double double room and requested the 37th floor when checking in, as I had read on this website that this particular floor had been recently renovated and the rooms were 'Premier'. The front desk staff were very nice and promptly upgraded us with no problems. The decor in the room was traditional but was extremely clean and was in no way shabby. The beds were extremely comfortable, there was a plasma tv, fridge, steam iron and board, safe and dressing gowns in the room also. The bathroom was pretty spacious, again, always clean, with new towels every day. We did leave a tip for the housekeeping staff every day, just 2 or 3 dollars and we definitely got excellent service from them. I had read that some people had problems with the lifts but we never had to wait more than a minute for them. We contacted the Concierge the 2nd morning and asked her to book some restaurants for us during our stay, we gave her a price range that we were willing to pay and the type of food we like. We arrived back in our room that evening to find a voicemail from her detailing the reservations, we weren disappointed at all with her choice. All in all, we honestly had no problems with the hotel and would definitely return. It is only a 5-10 minute walk from Times Square, Central Park etc. and right beside Grand Central and the Chrysler building.

<Content>great location we recently spent 3 nights in New York.The hotel is in a great location, a short walk to Times Square and the hop on hop off bus.The staff were extremely helpful from arrival onwards until we left.The room was clean, and the breakfast in the resturant was great(a little expensive with the exchange rate). <Author>Arthaus
<Content>New York Gem My wife and another couple of friends stayed at the hotel between Saturday 21st - 26th October 2006. Upon our arrival, there was a problem with our booking, however the staff dealt with the issue in a competent and timely manner, even allowing us into our rooms before the scheduled time......And what a room. We were in Room 3605 which presented us with the most glorious view of The Chrysler Building and the surrounding skyline. The size of the room was more than adequate with an extremely comfortable bed, flatscreen TV and lovely soft towels in the bathroom. There is also a safe, iron (and board) and a hair dryer. The room would benefit from tea-making facilities.Overall, the staff couldn't have been any more helpful, and this included a bottle of champagne left in our room with the hotel's compliments to help celebrate my wife and I's joint 50th birthdays. The Concierge was also very helpful with information about local tours, arranging transport to the airport and confirming flight times etc. The hotel is also in a great location, a short walking distance from Grand Central and the Chrysler Building. We didn't eat in the hotel, but found very good breakfasts next door at Pax, around the corner at The Frontier and for more of a dining experience, The Pershing Square Central Cafe opposite Grand Central.We would definitely stay there again.

<Content>Fitness Center is almost ready!! The Helmsley has recently renovated its rooms. Everything has been updated but the old air conditioning system is still there. For my stay, they had already switched to winter mode, so if you encounter Indian Summer as I did, with outside temperatures above normal, you're going to sweat inside your room!Also, the renovations either did not involve changing the beds or the hotel chose to install very poor quality beds. <Author>Marcus_Laz
<Content>Don't get over-excited In the last 4 years my wife and I have travelled some 48,000 miles around the world. We've stayed in some very impressive places and feel that we have enough experience to justifiably offer a critique of any hotel we encounter. The NY Helmsley is an OK hotel. It's good good staff, it's efficient, clean enough and has a decent bar and restaurant. If you don't expect any more than that you won't be disappointed. It's very convenient for all the sights and sounds of this incredible city and it's a true reflection of the people and the ambience itself. New York is a loud, bustling metropolis, where people live in the fast lane while trying to survive and make a living. Tourists are obviously welcome and well catered for but this is a living, breathing monster so if it's your first time be prepared to accept that New Yorkers have a unique 'style' in keeping with their surroundings. We had no complaints as such. Sure the rooms are smaller than any other in the US but this is New York - space on the island is at a premium so you'll just have to accept that. The people are great - laugh off the abrupt ones and join in with the colourful ones - this is what makes your trip anyway so enjoy it no matter what happens! You can't really go wrong at the Helmsley for a mid-priced base. We would recommend it to anyone.

<Author>littlecoyote
<Content>Two Star Hotel Let me start by saying that everyone on staff was very nice. Everything else about this hotel wasn't so great. It's two stars, maybe 2.5. Although the copy on the Expedia site has been changed -- no doubt due to me -- one of the reasons I booked this hotel was for complimentary wireless service. If you are on the lower floors it's all dial up. If you're on an upper floor, it's a dsl cable that isn't operational. At least it wasn't working in the room I was in, which featured a spaghetti of wires beneath the desk, not all of which were hooked up. An IT person was supposed to come up to the room to fix things while I was out but apparently never showed. I was, however, told there was free wifi in Bryant Park just three blocks away... (Bryant Park is by the Library between 5th  6th - it's lovely place -- also where they hold Fashion Week).You can access wifi in the hotel's Business Center, but they charge a chunk. Beyond all that, the place was falling apart and on the wrong side of shabby. In the renovated room I was moved to: 1) There was garbage in the trash can by the desk2) Three lightbulbs in the cut glass fixture around the mirror in the bathroom were burned out3) The hot water knob on the sink was missing a finishing piece4) The sink drain was an extremely slow drainer... 5) And scrawled onto the interior shower curtain were the words Too Short. Too Short. True, but even worse with the scribbles. When I decided to do some evening ironing so I wouldn't be so hurried in the morning before a meeting, I first thought the iron wasn't working. It turned out that the bottom outlet in the two-plug outlet I plugged into was dodgy. The top plug apparently worked because a lit lamp was plugged into it. My room had two beds so, given everything, I analyzed them closely before deciding which one to get into. One bed was rather poorly made, with a dust ruffle askew. I opted for bed #2, I don't know how anyone thinks this is a clean hotel. There's chipped paint, bad seals, spots on unholstery and carpets. It made me wonder whether some of the reviews I've read were plants. Having visited New York mostly for business many times, and stayed all over the island, I can tell you with absolute assurance that you can do better. Next time, I certainly will...I tried the Helmsley because the reviews sounded good, I'm always looking for new places (depending on the season, NY can book up so it's nice to have options), and 3.5 stars for a mid-price hotel was impressive. Beyond the location, which is convenient, especially if you want to catch the bus shuttle to LaGuardia across the street from Grand Centrel, this hotel is a bust. Keep looking...

<Content>Good hotel I've just got back after a five night stay. I was on the 10th floor in what I assume is not a newly decorated room. The hotel is in a good location, and I'd like to recommend the food court at Grand Central Station, which is a few minutes' walk away. <Author>Bryno
<Content>Great location, great staff, would go back tomorrow ! Stayed there for 5 nights in September 2006. Three of us sharing a room on the 39th Floor.It's in a fantastic location, just a few mins walk from Grand Central Station and Chrysler Building. Bus Stop across the road will take you all the way across 42nd Street to the West side for access to any of the Piers. Uptown/Downtown trains are available at Grand Central Station subway. The room was very well presented. We had a lot of trouble with the new flat screen TV and had to phone 'Tech Support' a lot of times, but I cannot really fault this as I believe that the flatscreens had only recently been installed and there were some teething problems which will get sorted out. The room had a double and a single bed, nice size en-suite with loads of towels, hair drier and other necessities. Only one dressing gown, but I'm certain we could have asked for more if we had really wanted them. There was fridge and a safe, ironing board and iron (didn't get much use!!) The elevator took less than one minute to get from ground floor to 39th, so no holdups there and as there are 6 elevators, there was rarely a wait. The reception staff were very efficient, it only took about 3 minutes to check in and the same to check out. The front of house guys were very friendly. Right next door to the hotel a very good coffee shop called PAX, while a three minute walk took you to Duane Reade Pharmacy/convenience shop for anything you may have forgotten to bring along.There is a very nice bar called Harrys just off the foyer and also a very good restaurant called Mindys where breakfast prices were quite reasonable. We did not use Mindys as we wanted to check out the local diners. (Johns, 45th street - very good, Comfort Diner, 46th Street - great, Brooklyn Diner, 57th Street - spectacular, though twice the price of the others)Our room was a 'Premier' room and it was slightly more expensive than standard but the few dollars more was well worth it. For anyone a little nervous of heights, you should make this known on booking so that they will allocate you a room on the lower floors.We had a most enjoyuable stay in NYC and the NY Helmsley played a major part in this. I didn't want to leave, but unfortunately c'est la vie.I'll be back, hopefully sooner rather than later.

<Author>txsmiles
<Content>Good Hotel, if you get a deal After extensive research, we booked at the Helmsley for a 5 day vacation. The good news - it is in a GREAT location, as previously mentioned walking distance from many things you'll want to do, and easy access to transportation at Grand Central, and of course an endless supply of taxi's outside the door on 42nd street. The hotel was clean, the rooms were spacious (really very large by NYC standards) We had a small refridgerator, which was a nice surprise. We did NOT have a flat screen TV or free internet access as mentioned by some. No coffee pot, either. The decor was outdated, and a bit shabby... but not enough to bother us. We could see the Chrysler building and weren't particularly bothered by noise from 42nd street... it IS New York, after all! All but one staff member were very friendly, helpful, and not demanding about tips. Unfortunately the one bad apple was a manager who very nearly ruined our trip before it started.The bad news - Do NOT expect to park an oversize vehicle at this hotel. Our multiple phone calls to confirm that they could park our van (at their ridiculous rate of $42.50 per day, no in-and-out priviledges) still resulted in them sending me, a single mother, out at 11pm to find our own place to park (thus, the bad-apple manager experience, noted above). This manager's attitude and behavior, especially after we had confirmed twice that they could accomodate our van, were outrageous. In addition, we had hot water issues (rather, a lack of hot water) and called twice a day for maintenance. No one showed up and we were not offered another room. If you can get a good rate, aren't concerned about staying in a trendy or chic hotel, want to be in mid-town, and don't need to park a large van... this is a good bet in NYC - booking through the hotel's website, we paid under $165 per night for 2 queen beds, ate several breakfasts from the PAX next door, and had a great vacation.  
<Date>Aug 21, 2006

<Author>rock1
<Content>Nice Three Star Hotel We just returned from a 3 night stay during a major New York heat wave-temperatures in the 100's. I am happy to say that the air conditioning worked beautifully! There was a minor glitch at check-in when they inquired if I had cancelled my reservations, but all was well, and we ended up with 2 adjoining rooms with a rollaway bed as requested. (We are a family of 5). The room with 2 double beds could accomodate a rollaway, which tells you that the room sizes were generous. We stayed on the 10th floor which was NOISEY. I am surprised this has not been mentioned more often--sirens were quite constant. I do not know if a higher floor would have helped, but when making reservations ask about the quiet side of the hotel. We also did not have the flat screen TV's I have seen mentioned, so if that is important to you, request one. Pax, the deli next door was perfect for breakfast to go. We did take our own coffee pot-although I was told complimentary coffee was available in the lobby from 6-8am. Bottom line-a nice basic hotel-nothing to write home about, but very satisfactory-and an excellent price by New York standards.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Value Central Hotel We stayed for 4 nights at the New York Helmsley in June. We got a good deal booking through Octopus Travel for a central New York hotel. The Helmsley was very good value for money for a centrally located 4 star hotel as we paid nearly as much 5 years ago for a 2 star.We got a room on the top floor which was spacious and although at the back of the hotel had nice views over towards the Empire State Building. The bathroom was quite good compared to most hotels in the UK and US - quite clean. I would agree that earplugs are a must as the air conditioning is quite noisy and there are always yellow cabs blowing their horns during the night! Our room had a flat screen tv and a fridge which came in useful.The hotel is ideally located close enough to walk to most attractions and only a few steps away from Central Station for those wanting alternative modes of transport. We found taxis fairly cheap and plentiful.We found the staff pleasant enough although we didn't have much contact other than checking in and out. The bellman was helpful enough when asked to keep our bags after check out until we were picked up for going back to the airport. The bar can be a bit of a pain as the staff are usually a bit evasive and they won't take orders at the bar or let you pay at the bar so it can somethimes be a bit of a wait.We went for breakfast at the Pax next door but I would avoid the pancakes as these are simply microwaved and not very fresh tasting. We found a great deli round the corner - Old Bridge (I think!) where you choose and buy your food downstairs and then there's a huge seating area upstairs. It was really fresh food and smoothies and only cost pennie - it seemed a bit daunting at first but its worth it. It was a pity we found it on our last morning.For dinner when we didn't want to venture far we went across the road from the hotel to an Italian, Osteria Laguna (I think). It was quite nice food with Italian rather than US portions so a bit of a lighter bite.  
<Date>Jul 10, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A fantastic base for New York City The New York Helmsley is a fantastic hotel in an ideal location in midtown Manhattan. We were made very welcome by Bernardo at reception who gave myself and five nursing colleagues rooms on the 37th floor. The rooms were very plush indeed with fabulous tempura mattresses and plasma TV screens and free email. The view from our room was awesome with the crysler building being on the left and the united nations being to the right. The staff were very attentive to your needs and despite comments from previous visitors of hands out for tips, we never saw this at all. The Door Staff were amazing and the two that shone for us were Nic and Michael, who were always smilling and ready to help with any query we had. They made getting about in Manhattan so much easier, and were so courteous and polite. The location is central for all subways and locations in middle Manhattan and as far as we were concerned was terrific value for money.If we are ever fortunate enough to be in New York again then we would have no hesitation in making The New York Helmsley our accomodation. It is a superb hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>What a surprise Having read some previous reviews I was very nervous about my stay in the Helmsley and arrived fearing the worst. However, from the moment I walked to reception to when I checked out, I could not find a reason to complain. The Hotel is ideally located for whatever or wherever you need to do and see. With the location comes the noise from the street but it was not an issue in the rooms. The rooms are spacious and clean, good shower and no hassles with a/c. The black out blinds are great too if you have had a long overnight flight before arrival. Breakfast is pricey but with plenty of cool little deli's and coffee shops nearby, why eat in the hotel. All in all, this is a great place to stay and I hope to return soon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great hotel We stayed at the Helmsley for 4 nights over the Memorial Holiday. At check in we were greeted by the friendly staff and we able to check in early (around 1). We were upgraded without asking and had a lovely veiw of the Empire State Building. We were on the 37th floor and only experience problems with the lifts 1 morning. The room was spacious  the beds were very comfortable. We had 2 small problems while staying there. The A/C unit did not work very well, we keep it running the whole time  it never got really cold. It was cool but the weather was not really hot while we were there. I would have second thoughts of staying during the heat of summer. Secondly the hot water in the shower was minumial. Had to take showers with almost no cold water on the get it hot enough. Overall it was a nice hotel, with friendly staff  very clean. We did dine in the hotel bar one night, it was good food, but pricey. We also took the advice of the forum and had breakfast at the PAX. Drinks were overpriced there but food was good. We really like the location, being close to Grand Central. I would stay at this hotel again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overatted like the rest of New York I stayed at this hotel with my family fromthe 23rd May. Like everything else in New York I left this htel with the feeling that I had not recieved good service or value for money. The room itself was OK with a good view of the Chrysler building. There were several annoyances with it though. Firstly it was nearly impossible to sleep with the noise from the traffic, horns and sirens going all night long. We were on the 29th floor yet it was just as noisy as being at street level, why the room doesn't have double glazing to reduce the noise, beggars believe.Another annoying thing was the TV. It was stored in a cabinet. The cabinet doors would only open a small amount, so basically if you weren't directly in front of the screen you couldn't see it from any other angle in the room. We had a double bed and only one person laying on the bed could see the screen. We had an early morning call at 6 am even though we didn't arrange this. I'm certain this was arranged on the automated system by the cleaners in our room as we hadn't left a tip in our room every day. We had every intention of leaving them a tip on the last day, but due to this incident they got nothing. The hotel tried to charge us for room service even though we had nothing, again I think this was the cleaners ordering something from our room.When I told the staff at the front desk about these incidents, they were very indifferent and gave me the impression that this sort of thing goes on all the time.There was no tea or coffee facilities in the room, and no breakfast included in the price.For 200 a night I feel this hotel was a complete rip off, although that goes for everything in Manhatten over priced and over rated, glad to get out the place in the end.Top tips, ask for a room thats away from the street, if you want a good view then you gotta suffer the noise that goes with it. Take breakfast at Pax's deli next door, it's not the greatest, but the prices are resonable for Manhatten.Buy all your snacks, crisps, biscuits and drinks from Duane Reade ( 100 yrds away ), turn left out of hotel and then right, it's on the far corner. A 2 litre bottle of water from the Deli costs $4.00. Where as at Duane reade 4 litres will cost $1.00.Be prepared to get ripped off all over the city. I'm surprised they don't tax the air. Also you got to tip everyone for everything, they've all got their hands out for something and if you don't give them it, they'll ask for it. Nice to go once, but never again.  
<Date>May 29, 2006

<Author>JoanButler
<Content>Great Hotel for First Visit to New York My son and I travelled to New York for a weekend May 11 and I did extensive research on hotels before deciding on the New York Helmsley because of its location, features and price. Thanks to Trip Advisor I had a comfort level with the hotel and location but having read so much about small rooms and other issues with New York hotels I admit I was still a little apprehensive.We were able to check in very quickly and staff friending, although we were not given any information on any features of the hotel. We were very pleased with our double room and its amenities. We were on the 37th floor and except for the faint noise of the constant horn blowing in New York, the hotel was exceptionally quiet. The location was fabulous - away from the hustle of Times Square yet within walking distance of everything and close to subway which we used to get to and from Yankees games. The only thing missing was a coffee maker in the room, but we did have a fridge. I will certainly go back there again and recommend it.

<Content>Great Hotel and Great Staff Having stayed in New York a number of times I have known only too well how terrible hotels can be, and so I was very pleasantly surprised to find that the Helmsley was a great place to stay.We stayed for 7 seven nights but by the second we already knew a number of the staff by name and I was greeted personally each time I entered the lobby. All in all I would reccomend this hotel and will stay again on my next trip.. especially if I can get the same great deal I got through Escape Travel here in Aus!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel Stayed at the helmsley for 5 nights with 4 friends, rooms are suprisingly spacious for a city hotel. We had 2 double beds, a plasma screen and a fridge. A very good price for a 4* hotel in a very central location. We also hired a roll away bed for $30 per night which was like a proper bed with wheels...The hotel location is brilliant....a short walk from 5th avenue shopping, the empire state building and timesquare. The closest underground station is Grand Central Station. We got a cab frm JFK...with there being 5 of us we ordered from a private hire firm - 'carmel' and payed $70 inc tips and toll.Some of the hotel staff do come across a little roud and somewhat impersonal. The shower was a little annoying as the water was either a little too warm or a little too cold and it did take a while sometimes to adjust to the right temperature. Aside from that cant fault the hotel. Rooms were made everyday and copy of new york times was delivered daily. The concierge are very helpful and provided all sightseeing info.If you're vegetarian I would warn you that there is a general limited variety in new york city. We lived off subway and dominos pizza for the week....Would definitely stay at the helmsley again....great time in new york.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Superb!!! This was our first time in New York so we were a bit nervous of what to expect especially with regard to our hotel. We were so impressed with the hotel, we would definately recommend it. It was clean, by no means basic and centrally located. For the price we paid we were over joyed with our accomodation and would not fault it. It cost us about $60 in a taxi from JFK, that was including toll and tip which isn't bad. There is a bus which goes to and from the airport and stops at Grand Central Station which is literally a 10 minute walk up the street which is about $13 each. If you are lazy (like us)there are always taxis right outside of the hotel. Next door to the hotel is a place called Pax which offers a selection of food and drink which is really handy for breakfast or a coffee. I could not comment on the hotel food as we did not eat there once! We thoroughly enjoyed our time in New York and having a good hotel really helped. If you are planning a trip on a budget definately stay at this hotel because I can guarantee you will not be dissapointed. The only fault I could possibly find is the time you have to wait for lifts, but I reckon that is standard in NY as everything is so high!

<Author>EddieT
<Content>Great location, some rooms okay I booked my room through a no-name site who offered prices well below retail (paid $850 for 4 nights for two people). The first company I reserved with said they could not sell them to me, the place was booked. I tried again with another firm, and this time got a room. A month before we were scheduled to arrive, I called to verify the room reservation, and also request a recently renevated room, non-smoking. They confirmed, and put in the requests. Once we arrived, we were given room 2616. It was fairly high, so I figured it was exactly what I ordered..it wasn't! It was a smoking room, on a smoking floor, with two double beds. The TV was standard, and the room had some stains (floor, bedsheet, etc). As the belhop unloaded the luggage I called down to complain, and request another room. I was told the place was full (couldn't tell by the # of people), and that they didn't even have any rooms with a single bed. After a few more minutes of repeating my requests, she'd check and call back. 5 minutes later she (manager) said housekeeping said there was a room we could transfer to. This one was on the 16th floor - 1605. While it WAS on a non-smoking floor, someone definately smoked in it. There were cigarette burns on the bedsheet, and the place reeked worse. The belhop moved our stuff, but when my (now) fiance got there she almost threw up it was so bad. I called downstairs to complain again, and was told again there were no rooms - the room we just moved to they moved the guy to our original room on 26. I continued to complain about it, threatened to sue, requested a refund so we could go elsewhere...etc... Finally she mentions that the soonest they could do anything would be in the morning, and to give up our room early, then they'd have something later...so we opened the window, turned up the heater, and went out for the night.When we got back it was a little better, but still way too obvious. I even considered having them hold my luggage downstairs so the smoke wouldn't permeate the clothes. Nevertheless, we slept, and in the morning packed back up, gave up our room, were told they'd upgrade us, so we left for the morning and trusted God.Around noon we got back to change for the opera, and were told we had been moved to the 33rd floor. This was good news for me, because I know the higher floors had been renovated...and sure enough, we had a corner room, with flat screen TV, single king bed, and a dresser. Plenty of room, awesome view towards downtown - could even see the Brooklyn Bridge.The location is excellent - a block to the first subway entrance, 2 blocks to Grand Central.All in all I was satisfaied, but not enough to go back. I'll pay extra for a decent room anyday.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel, great location! Have just returned from New York 2 days ago and spent 5 nights at the Helmsley along with my parents. This was my second time in New York as I loved it so much the first time round. The hotel is conveniently located by most of the amenities New York City has to offer. Most of the famous landmarks like Grand Central Station, Times Square, Empire State Building, Macys etc, are all in walking distance. We also emailed the hotel and asked for a higher floor, but did not get that as you have to pay extra. In any case, you really dont need to pay for a better room as the rooms are fine anyway. We were on the 10th floor, the room was very comfortable and spacious. I've never slept on a more comfy mattress as the ones they have on the beds, so nice to not wake up with a bad back like I do every morning at home! The only grumble we had was that the rooms do not have any tea or coffee making facilities, no kettles, nothing. The hotel has complimentary tea and coffee every morning in the reception, but when we wanted a hot drink at night we had to go next door to the Pax deli. The staff were all very nice, particularly the english doorman, don't know his name but he was from Hertfordshire and was really friendly and always had a smile on his face. The Pax deli next door to the hotel is great for a breakfast, I can't say that the staff were not nice like somebody else mentioned on here, because they were all ok with us. A tip NOT to go to is the Comfort Diner which is 3 blocks down on 45th Street, we went there for a breakfast on our 2nd morning, and the food was cold and overcooked, obviously heated up, and not nice at all. On the whole, the Helmsley is a wonderful Hotel in a wonderful place. I'd definitely stay there again in the future, hope to go back one day!  
<Date>Mar 9, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>OK but nothing special... Just got back after spending 5 nights at this hotel. Asked 10 months ago for a renovated room on a higher floor - got a room on the 10th. I think it was refurbished but couldn't be sure. At the back of the hotel but I had a decent view of the Empire State Building. Room was ok size wise with two Queen sized beds. Good location - only 5 minutes from Grand central Station. Reception staff were polite and helpful with no delay in checking in or out. No delays in getting a lift either as reported elsewhere. Bellhops were ok so long as you tipped them but the doorman (who was english like me) was downright rude - may as well get himself a begging bowl. Overall, I'd recommend the hotel but only if you get a good deal on the room rates.

<Content>great location and fine hotel we stayed at this hotel for 4 nights and are only just back. We thought the hotel was fine. Staff were generally very nice, we did not eat at the hotel and the bar is very small. But the area around the hotel is so laden with places to eat and drink. I would definately recommend staying at this hotel if you have a mid-range budget. We will stay again but next time, we will be non-smokers and possibly pay extra for a room higher up.

<Author>Papa Shep
<Content>Aussie Aussie Aussie Oi, Oi , Oi - Great location My wife, our 12 year old son and I checked in at the New York Helmsley on 17 January 2006 and checked out on 23 January 2006. 6 nights in total in New York for our holiday.We had booked through an internet site and didn't know what to expect. I emailed the hotel a few weeks before our visit to confirm that they had received our reservation. It did take the hotel 3 emails before they responded with a reservation number but it was still a week before our arrival. I did request a non smoking room on a high level and was advised they would do there best.We flew United airlines from Australia and our flight was expected to arrive at Newark at 8.00 p.m. on 17 January. All the United planes we flew on had mechanical problems resulting in us arriving in San Francisco 4 hours behind our connecting flight. United wanted to reschedule our flight to 10.30p.m San Francisco time meaning we would not arrive in New York until at least 7.00a.m. the next day. We kicked up and were seated on an earlier flight arriving at JFK just after midnight. We then arrived at our hotel around 1.30 a.m. in the morning and were greeted pleasantly by the front desk staff. We were told our room was on the 9th floor as they were booked out however we could pay US$50 per night for an upgrade. We declined. The gentleman who took our bags to our room was very friendly and we enjoyed our room. It was not an overly large room but was more than adequate for our needs. The bathroom was a very good size. The bed and the pillows were a bit soft for our liking and coming from the other side of the world our body clocks were all over the place. We had difficulty sleeping because of our excitement being in New York!We could hear the garbage collection going on during the night but it wasn't load and we got used to it.Our window was facing the office building next door so we didn't have a good view of the city as we had hoped.I was disappointed that our room did not have a fridge or a safe.The front desk has safety boxes for valuables that we used and this was pretty easy to use.When we left the hotel the next day we could see how close we were to everything!Grand Central 5 minute walk.United Nations 10 minute walkCentral Park 30 minute walkEmpire State Building 15 minute walkTimes Square 15 minute walkDowntown 5 minute walk 10 minute subway trainQuality affordable restaurants breakfast and dinner5 minutesEverything is close by and New York is a safe comfortable city to walk around.We did have breakfast in the restaurant one morning. The food was nice but the waiters were a bit stuck up and not all that friendly.The hotel security people were very discrete and friendly in their manner as was most staff at the hotel.There were a lot of airline staff and diplomats staying there.One difficulty staying on the 9th floor occurred every morning if you wanted to use the elevators. As people from higher floors were checking out the elevators rarely stopped on the lower floors for pick ups. We ended up walking down the stairs on one occasion. The stairs led us to the executive office and there was no clear signage to make it back to the lobby. We had a bit of fun with this as staff saw us walking around the executive office area and asked if they could help us. We told them thank you as the CEO has approved all their pay rise requests.Overall we paid AU$210 Australian dollars (about US$170) a night for the 3 of us to stay at the New York Helmsley.We felt we received value for our money as the hotel was clean and safe. The house keeping was very good replacing towels and toiletries each day.The room did get warm but when I opened a window it was very pleasant.The New York temperature for our stay was unusually mild (low-mid 50's) making it ideal for walking around this great city and returning to a comfortable clean room.As we had stayed at the Stanford Hotel on 32nd street last year, I would say that both hotels are equal except that the staff at the Helmsley is friendlier.We would recommend this hotel for people on holidays to stay because of its location and value for money high standards.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beat My Expectations I am used to tiny hotel rooms in NYC that cost $400/night and involve sleeping with your feet dangling off of the bed, jammed against the dresser, and waking up and rolling into the wall due to lack of room. The New York Helmsley definitely exceeded my expectations. Our 37th floor room had a spectacular view of the city, a plasma TV, two FULL sized beds, a large bathroom, and all of the trimmings that you expect at a midrange hotel OUTSIDE of NYC, but learn to live without at a sub $200 night spot in Manhattan.The one complaint was the check in time. The line was out the door, and they had one, slow as molasses, clerk checking people in. We had to reschedule our dinner due to the AWFUL wait. They had other clerks that seemed to be standing around and not helping to aleviate the long line, which made things even worse.Overall, a great value and I will stay there again. When you find a hotel with large clean rooms, that is centrally located in midtown, for under $150/night, you stick with it.

<Author>Kellbo
<Content>Good Stay At The Helmsley I stayed at the Helmsley during my first trip to New York so my review is independent from comparison to other hotels in the area. On the whole I was pleased with my stay.The Hotel has an extremely good location, situated in Midtown New York on East 42nd Street. It is away from the hustle and bustle of the busiest areas, yet still within easy walking distance to the Chrysler Building, Grand Central Station and Times Square. There is a subway station close by.Check in was efficient and trouble free and all staff around the lobby appeared to be cheerful and ready to help. The bell boy took our luggage right into our room and was very open to answering questions. The room itself was of sufficient size, with two double beds, two comfy chairs and a desk. The room and bathroom are fairly out dated and things are fairly worn around the edges, worn parts in the curtains, electric sockets lose from the walls etc. However, it was kept sufficiently clean by the maids which made up for this. I also believe that some of the Hotel has been refurbished and we happened to be in the older part. There were no tea/coffee facilities within the room. The hotel has two restaurants and room service facilities. Room service prices are pretty much as you expect-slightly higher than the average cost of a meal. The food however was of good quality and arrived promptly, within about 30 minutes. The New York Times was delivered each morning to our room. We were on the seventh floor and so there was noise from the traffic but this is to be expected in the city that never sleeps and wasn much of a problem for me. Security was fairly tight which was a bonus, on several occasions room keys had to be presented before being allowed to progress into the lifts. The hotel is about average value for money considering it within a city and has good location. All in all I was happy with the hotel, the staff were pleasant and efficient, location fantastic and the room was sufficient for somewhere to sleep after a hard days sightseeing!  
<Date>Dec 5, 2005

<Content>Recommended if you pay $200 or so a night Overall, this was a great stay. The beds and pillows were extremely comfortable. Our room was extremely clean everyday and the rooms were very large for a NYC hotel. We would stay there again.I recommend that you stay on the 38th floor. Our bedspreads and everything else was in great condition. Nothing was worn down like other people mentioned. We had a great view of the Chrysler building. I recommend that you book the hotel from www.crshotels.com. CRS hotels had the room for the same price as expedia but there were no additional fees and you don't pay until you leave. We paid $300 for a Saturday and $200 per night for a Sunday and Monday. I would not stay there for $300 a night for all three nights but our deal was a great one and we'd go there again. Location is excellent!I'd bring a fan or buy one though. We were kind of hot and had to keep the windows open at night. Even though the windows were open it was still very quiet since we were so high up. Overall, a great experience and a trip of a lifetime!

I can't tell you the cost per satisfaction ratio since the company picked up the tab, but it was a very pleasant experience. <Author>tensing
<Content>lovely hotel Have just returned from a 3 night stay at this hotel with three other girls and we were really impressed with everything about it.Its location was excellent being within walking distance of many attractions and the staff were all very friendly, polite and helpful. Our room on the 12th floor was clean, and comfortable with plenty of storage space and we were not disturbed by traffic noise (although we were not at the front of the building}. In reception we were able to change our dollar travellers cheques at no charge and we also had a safe deposit box again at no charge - both of these facilities were available to us 24hrs per day. On our last day we were able to leave our cases with a bell boy and collect them just before we left for the airport. We ate breakfast in the PAX diner right next door to the hotel which was very convenient, reasonably priced and of good quality. After a long tiring day we had a bar meal at the hotel and although not cheap the food was good. Spirit  mixers were about $8.50 but much larger than the measures in uk. Only critism would be that it would have been nice to have tea/coffee making facilities in room - free coffee/tea available in reception lobby but not available all day so we brought in from PAX next door if it was still open.

<Author>CharlieFrance
<Content>Big hotel in a great mid-town location We stayed at the New York Helmsley Hotel for one week in September 2005. The hotel had been recommended to us by a native New Yorker, so we reserved it from home on Expedia.Overall we were happy with our stay. The room was clean, spacious and had a big bathroom. The double bed was hard. There was a flat screen TV with Internet access. The real advantage of this hotel is it's location. It's a short walk to Grand Central Station. The neighbourhood is safe because the United Nations is only a couple of blocks away.Some of the lower floors of the hotel need to be refurbished ASAP. And the hotel parking lot is ridiculously expensive!!!This is a hotel with a lot of rooms and a high turnover of guests (airline crews stay here). If you want a more personal service you should stay in a smaller, boutique hotel.We found a traditional American Diner only 2 blocks way which serves a full American breakfast. It is called The Comfort Diner and it is located on 214 E 45TH St. Good value too.

<Content>Great hotel with class! <Content>Very pleasant stay and more than adequate First......to address earlier reviews, IF the ice machine is not on your floor, there is a clear sign in the hall directing you to the appropriate location....The staff did not at all appear ignorant to us - we found the front desk staff very pleasant and helpful, and the bell staff were more than adequate. I was very surprised by the room - much bigger than i expected for a Manhattan hottel room. Nicely appointed - though not space age chic. We were on the 9th floor, on the back, facing 41st street. Overall this hotel is a VERY good deal for the money in NYC. We would definitely stay there again. It always amazes me how persnickity many travelers have to be about accomodations - typical pampered, arrogant, American attitude when it comes to traveling. I'm in NYC to relish in the city and the culture, not my hotel room:)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Superb Stay My Boyfriend and I stayed at the New York Helmsley for 5 nights in November 2004. After searching the internet for a reasonably cheap holiday to New York, we came across this hotel. As this was to be our first time in New York we requested a king size bedroom with a good view. When we arrived, we were really happy with the appearance of the front of the hotel, with the bell boys outside opening the doors for us, made us feel important. Check in was very fast and efficient, considering there was about 20 virgin reps checking in at the same time. The receptionist was very pleasant and informed us she had upgraded us to an executive room at no extra charge. We were on the 41st floor (very top floor). On walking into the room, it was huge (for a hotel room). The bathroom was lovely decorated, as was the whole room. Our bed was huge, we had a flatscreen huge tv mounted onto the wall. The best bit was to come, we opened the curtains and the view of the Empire State Building was just amazing. The cleaners changed our towels everyday, and tidied our room when we had made a little mess. The bell boys were very informative. There was however two things we wasn so happy about. Although we took part in the New York ipping system?I did come across one rude bell boy. He carried our luggage on the last day to a store cupboard 2 feet away and would not give our tickets to us unless we tipped him and just stood there holding his hand out.Another thing to be aware off is the phone in the room. We did not intend on using the hotel phone. but our mobile phones would not work in New York, and the pay card we had purchased would not work either, we resorted to using the hotel phone to inform people back home we were there safe and well. You know what its like when your away you can never remember the international codes, then the code for dialling out of the USA. So after about 4 blank attempts at trying to phone home we eventually got through. What we wasn aware of for all the times we had dialled the wrong numbers we got charged for even though we never even spoke to anyone on the other end of the line. We spoke to the receptionist and informed her we would not be paying the $225 dollars they billed us for as we had not spoke to anyone. We only ended up paying for the 3 minute call we made, which we was much more satisfied with.I would definitely recommend this hotel for anyone of all ages. We are in our early 20 but anyone with standard and a bit of class like us would love and appreciate this hotel. Will hopefully be returning in the future. I shall add photos of Empire State building view from the window and pics of the hotel in the near future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't ask for a fan. It was probably nice the last time it was redecorated, which appeared to have been about 30 years ago. The room was unremarkable, very motel-like, perhaps because the TV was small and on a stand rather than in an armoire. Of the few outlets in the room, only the one into which the TV was plugged was actually accessible. The others required crawling on the floor or moving furniture, only to discover that the outlet might not actually work.The climate controls were rudimentary at best, and the AC seemed to run constantly no matter what the temperature setting. I asked for a fan, and housekeeping delivered a fan that had no knob. When I finally found a working outlet, and a pair of tweezers, I discovered that the knob was apparently missing because the fan did not work. I requested a second fan, and this one had a broken blade than sat at the bottom of the case and impeded the rotation of the other blades, which made the fan jump around like one of those cartoon alarm clocks. When I called Housekeeping a third time, they did not answer, so I took my fan to the lobby, where I was forced to circumnavigate the ridiculous late-night security features. These consisted of blocking the entrance to the elevators from the side of the lobby nearest the front desk, forcing people to walk all the way around the lobby for no apparent reason.However, the manager was able to convince Housekeeping to provide me with a non-damaged, functional fan.The beds were quite brick-like, and the pillows were uncomfortable for reasons that I cannot quite put my finger on.The tub had a tendency to back up during showering.Last but not least, there was an ice bucket, but there was no information regarding the location of the ice machine. I considered calling the front desk to ask, but I was tired after my adventure with the fan.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good time in Manhattan My wife and I have just returned from a week in the Helmsley Hotel in New York. We had a great time in the city and our experiences at the Helmsley contributed in no small way to our enjoyment of the Big Apple.The Hotel is centrally situated and is very close to Grand Central ; this was of special advantage to us as it is pretty easy to get to Grand Central from anywhere in the city.The staff in the Helmsley were helpful and courteous at all times ;when the elevators developed a problem on a busy Sunday morning,the staff facilitated guests through the use of the service lift,for instance. We were particularly impressed with the concierge service.We stayed in a Deluxe King bedroom and we both agree that the ambience of the room was excellent( We were at the top of the Hotel on floor 41 so traffic noises were within reason).If you haven't been in a big bed before, then this is the place to go! Room was cleaned every day,we got plenty of big and small towels and the New York Times arrived at our door every morning. The TV set was of high quality but we didn't get much time to sit and watch. The radio was good ( FM seems to focus on music and AM on talk shows in NY )One problem we had with the room was the lighting. It was difficult to read ; the table lamps proved good lighting for getting about generally but were not conducive to reading. It was difficult to read in bed....it is unfortunate that lights aren't provided over the bed to allow guests to read in comfort while resting in bed.We didn't take breakfast in the Hotel and we only had late night drinks on one occasion; the drinks were very expensive but the bar is very attractive. Although we didn't do it ,we were surprised to notice that guests are allowed to take food to their rooms.....for instance,I met a guest in the lift with a large pizza !! Coffee....very nice coffee..... was available in the foyer free of charge in the morning ; we are not sure if this is common practice in New York but it was a plus for us in this hotel.This hotel is a little expensive but ,on balance, it is worth it. We would stay here again .It is clean,has courteous staff and the bedrooms are attractive. We can certainly recommend it and give it an above average rating.  
<Date>May 18, 2005

<Content>Not ideal for business travelers Let me start out by saying that my perspective is that of a business traveler and the hotel does have some good points--it is good value for a NYC hotel in this hotel class (paid about $185 before taxes) and is well located (42nd and 3rd ave). This hotel must have been rather grand some years ago but, in my opinion, has fallen into some disrepair now. The staff does try to keep the rooms clean and that is a plus. However, I found the room rather shabby because it hasn't been kept up, the bedsheet was torn, the temperature control in tbe room was broken, had no hi-speed internet access, and the lighting in the hallway was dim and unappealing. I have stayed before at the Sheraton on Sixth Ave and for about $15 more, had a great room in a spotless hotel--unfortunately the hotel was sold out this time. Will never return to this hotel if I can help it.

<Author>GVTV
<Content>Good location, clean hotel and friendly staff Stayed at the hotel 3-5 April 2005.Very happy with the location - only 5 mins walk to Grand Central Station which has a shuttle service to Times Square about every 5 mins and just a few minutes ride. Clean hotel with friendly staff. Harry's bar is defintely a good place to eat. Quite a good bar menu and not anyway as expensive as Mindy's restaurant. Room was fine - beds comfortable, iron and ironing board provided. Bathroom larger than thought it would be with good toiletries and big fluffy towels!Quite a lot of noise in the rooms from the traffic below and we were on the 28th floor!Didn't eat in the restaurant - $18 for breakfast. There is a deli next door called PAX. Very clean cafe and very friendly staff. They do a standard breakfast of omelette, breakfast potatoes and toast or sausages or bacon, breakfast potatoes, eggs and toast for 3.75 - also a choice of breakfast sandwiches.They also have fruit bowls, choice of dried cereals, english muffins and yoghurt to choose from - all reasonably priced. They also do lunch menus sandwiches, wraps and soups and salads - again all good value for money. The only problem we had was checking out. We had to check out at 12:00 but were not getting picked up until 18:00 as our flight was 21:30 that night. We left our luggage with the doorman for storage. However, when we asked for our luggage to be retreived as our taxi had arrived it took them 15 mins to get back to us - not good when you have a taxi waiting outside.Anyway, all in all I would definitely stay in this hotel again.
