<Author>Nick_C_London
<Content>Very Good Hotel, Great Value for Money March 15 to 22 2005. Party of 4, two rooms on 8th floor, booked through expedia @ UK90 per night (US$166.50) including all taxes.Summary: Very good quality, great value for money, would def stay there again and recommend it. Expedia rate it 3.5*, I'd give it 4.5*. Great deal through Expedia - could have paid slightly more for a high floor executive room on the hotel's own web site.Pros: Friendly and helpful staff, large clean rooms, lots of towels and good toiletries. Iron and ironing board. 3 phones, cheap local calls from room. Reasonable range of TV channels plus pay to view movies. Great location.Cons: Low floor (8th) on 42nd St - a little traffic noise during the rush hours but no great problem for us and quiet at night. Blinds don't open/close easily - need replacing, but curtains open/close easily giving complete black out at night. Carpet a little worn and could do with replacing, but these unrefurbished rooms are much better than I had expected from other reviews on this page. No in room safe in standard rooms. No international or foreign language TV channels - no world news channels - even CNN was domestic, typically American!Commentary: 4 guests with lots of luggage. Not offered help with luggage on arrival. Very friendly check in. Rooms a pleasant surprise, large clean and comfortable - old fashioned but cheerful decor in generally good condition. Plenty of storage and hanging space.Oblique view of Chrysler from room at front (42nd st) and a better view of the Empire State from friends' room at back (43rd st). Cocktail bar good value for money for us Brits as the  is strong right now. Waitress had a dry sense of humour - loved her. 15% service added to bar bill automatically and highlighted - very honest and reasonable. Strawberry Daiquiri's very artificial and not very strong. Good bar snacks; free hors d'oeuvres during happy hour (5pm to 7pm).Tipped the bell captain a dollar a bag for looking after our 8 cases on checkout, and tipped another dollar a bag to a different guy when we retrieved them. Tipped the doorman $5 for loading them into the taxi. All seemed quite happy, and you expect to have to tip in these situations.Deli next door has excellent food, but self service and quite busy.Andrew's coffee shop on 43rd near the side of Grand Central very cheap, good American breakfast, friendly service. Pershing Square (under the road bridge over 42nd outside Grand Central) very good quality food (real maple syrup!) but poor luke warm coffee, slow service, and 3 times the price of Andrew's!Strongly recommend El Rio Grande just 4 blocks south on 3rd and 38th - Tex/mex with the best (and strongest!) margaritas in town.

<Author>sendmehome
<Content>Good Hotel but not for business travellers Rooms were well decorated, spacious for NY standards, clean and had fluffly towels. The bathrooms were nicely done. The deli next door is wonderful with bacon,eggs,homefries and toast for $3.75. However the hotel has no interent access. You can use the business center at $7 for 15 minutes or local phone calls are $1.00 for 3 minutes at .15 for each additional minute. There are no desks in the rooms. If you need to talk in the lobby, seating is very limited. While hotel is two blocks from Grand Central, there are limited restaurants within walking distance (in cold weather anyway) and very little shopping. Be prepared to take cabs. The hotel has free coffee in the lobby in the morning, but again seating is very limited. Don't eat at Harry's Bar as the sandwiches are terrible and way over priced. However if you get a good rate, this is an upscale hotel.  
<Date>Jan 29, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Location, nice hotel, some rude staff We stayed at the New York Helmsley Nov 19-21, 2004. Check in was a fairly painless process, however the checkin staff worked very slowly it took me 10 mins to check in and there was only one person in front of me. Eventually a second person came and checked me in. The room was nice and as requested we had 2 double beds. The decor was outdated but the room was clean and the towels were very fluffy and nice!!The only problem that we ran into was extremely rude bell captain. Since we had a late flight we asked that our luggage be kept at the hotel and the conceriege told us the bell captain would be happy to keep it. There was a huge line to leave our luggage, since our flight wasn't until 8PM we needed the luggage to be kept until 5PM, when we left the luggage the bell captain told us he wouldn't be here at 5, held out his hand (for a tip) and then told us he would have to store our luggage upstairs. He was abrupt and very rude. When we returned at 5 he was there expecting another tip when he sent a bellhop for the luggage then ignored our request for a cab. We went outside and one of the bell hops was happy to get us a cab. Other than the very rude bell captain, our stay was good. If I got a good deal in the future I would stay again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great but no kettle! We visited the New York Helmsley, 42nd Street, NYC in August 2004 - 2 adults, 1 teenager. Great Hotel, jaded is some respects but grand and glitzy enough to retain a glamorous feel to it. Think Dallas, and gold bathrooms, and you won't go far wrong! Large room, definitely bigger than the NYC average.. and huge fluffy towels. Great location too.. a couple of blocks from Grand Central Station, ten minutes on foot into Times Square, and we had a view to DIE for of the beautiful Chrysler Building from our room. Ask for a room with a view when you book.. it worked for us! What we didn't like was not having tea/coffee making facilities.... unusual for NYC, in fact unusual for any hotel, and it struck us as being rather greedy, especially as room service and in house refreshment was expensive. Take a travel kettle with you, and take breakfast at the local Deli's.. they are good value. Harry's bar is legendary, at least the Martinis are.. and they deserve to be! One is enough to put most people under the table.. two, and you won't know which City you are in. This was my second trip to NYC, a City I love. I would choose the New York Helmsley again for its price range, location, friendly feel and gold glitzy bathroom... and particularly for the Martinis! But.. TAKE A KETTLE!  
<Date>Nov 26, 2004

<Author>Whinbrook
<Content>Great Location, Shame about the Rooms Have just returned from 5 nights at The New York Helmsley Hotel. We had two rooms on what appeared to be unrefurbished floors (8th and 9th floors, so beware!). All the previous comments on this hotel about tired, shabby, dated decor applies to our stay, so we were not too surprised or too disappointed and we paid a bargain price ($175 per room per night inclusive) on a consolidators web site. Had we paid full rack rate, we would have raised hell as the rooms were well passed their sell by date decor wise. We have stayed in 4 and 5 star hotels in the USA on many occassions and there are some amenities missing from the rooms that we expected at a 4 star hotel as this Helmsley property is graded as. However, despite all this, the hotel is in an excellent location, the staff we came across were friendly and accommodating (house keeping came to one of our rooms on several occassions to fix broken fittings and were very efficient and polite) the complimentary coffee in the lobby was welcome, the bathroom toiletries were good quality and the towels were also very good. We never tried the restaurant but it looked an attractive space with a good if ordinary menu. The hotel was very busy through out our stay and each morning the lift service could not cope with the number of guests and we found ourselves either waiting well over 10 minutes to get into a lift to the ground floor or we had to walk down the fire stairs which became very irritating.It would be interesting to see a refurbished room, we strayed onto a refurbished floor (10th) and the corridors looked quite attractive (and with no kitchen smell from the a/c ducts). Even so, for the next trip to NYC we shall spend the extra to stay in a more modern, better equipped and decorated property.

<Content>A fantastic Hotel !!! I have only today returned from our trip to New York City. It was my first trip to the city so was not too sure what to expect. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised After reading many reviews, I was expecting an old, dirty, and not up to date hotel. Instead I was surprised the minute I saw the place. Compared to most nyc hotels, it was large and had a driveway where you could unload luggage. The lobby was very busy, but did not have many places to sit and rest. When we checked in, we were given an upgrade to a room that normally costs $499; we paid $209. The room was large with two queen beds, extremely clean, a view of the empire state building, and had very luxurious linens and exceptional towels, large and fluffy. We did not eat there nor have drinks, but the lounge was busy each time we went by. The clerk at the front desk was attentive and friendly. I dont know what the lower level room look like or have for amenities, but the upstairs is great. Most of the clientele were older, but there were many young people, with and without families. I would give it another try and hope for another upgrade. thanks

<Content>Comfortable with questionable service I recently returned from a three-day weekend stay and would recommend this hotel to anyone who wants a spacious, clean room with a comfortable bed. <Author>pumpkin31
<Content>Perfect! Stayed here for 4 nights in june and had a wonderful time. It was our first time to new york and I had spent ages researching before eventually settling for the New York Helmsley - I'm glad to say I picked well and got good value for money (100 sterling room rate per night - booked on OctopusTravel). As other tripadvisor users point out the hotel decor is in 1980s mode but dont let this put you off - the rooms are extremely spacious and clean (which I understand is unusual for new york) - we had two queen beds in our room on th 33rd floor - with a fantastic view of the new york skyline and chrysler building just opposite. There was also a fridge and tea and coffee making facilities. Location is excellent being a 2 min walk from grand central station (v handy for subway). Also grand central has an excellent food court where we often picked up a tasty and reasonable breakfast. Times square is also only 5-10 min stroll. Didn't eat in the hotel during our stay-however they did serve tasty complimentary hor d'oeurves from 5pm-7pm each night in the bar. Will definitely be back!!
